Requirement of Witness Agreement in Wording and Meaning
Intra-Hanafi dispute on witness agreement condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for witness testimony agreement and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the degree of verbal correspondence required.

Core Idea
Witness testimony requires literal or synonymous agreement, not just shared implication.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a critical condition for accepting witness testimony in Hanafi fiqh. The matn states that witnesses must agree in wording and meaning, but the commentary reveals a nuanced intra-madhhab dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (the Sahibayn). Understanding this condition—and the precise definition of 'agreement in wording'—is essential for evaluating testimonial evidence in Islamic courts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition from the matn
Read the matn statement: 'And agreement of the two witnesses in wording and meaning is required.' This is the baseline condition. Note that it is a condition (shart) for acceptance, not a pillar or integral.
2
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The commentary attributes the strict requirement of both wording and meaning to Abu Hanifa, while the Sahibayn hold that agreement in meaning alone suffices. Identify the practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, divergent amounts or words cause rejection; under the Sahibayn, the common element is accepted.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
3
Analyze the key distinction: wad' vs tadammun
The commentary clarifies that 'agreement in wording' means the two utterances convey the same meaning by way of proper signification (wad'), not by way of implication (tadammun). Two words like 'khaliyya' and 'barriyya' both imply divorce, but they are not synonyms, so testimony is rejected. However, synonyms like 'hiba' and 'atiyya' or 'nikah' and 'tazwij' are accepted.
This distinction resolves an apparent contradiction with al-Nihaya.
4
Apply the rule to examples
Work through the examples: multiple witnesses testifying to different amounts (1,2,3,4,5 dirhams) — Abu Hanifa rejects all, Sahibayn accept 4. Testimony to usurpation vs confession of usurpation — rejected because the subjects differ (substantive act vs evidentiary fact).
Focus on the illa (effective cause) for each ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ويعتبر اتفاق الشاهدين لفظاً ومعنى أي عند أبي حنيفة رضي الله عنه، عندهما الاتفاق في المعنى والمراد باتفاقهما لفظاً تطابق لفظيهما على إفادة المعنى بطريق الوضع لا بطريق التضمن فلو ادعى على آخر مائة درهم فشهد واحد بدرهم وآخر بدرهمين وآخر بثلاثة وآخر بأربعة وآخر بخمسة لم تقبل عنده في شيء لعدم الموافقة لفظاً، وعندهما يقضى بأربعة. وكذا إن شهد أحدهما بألف والآخر بألفين لم تقبل عنده، وعندهما تقبل على الألف إذا كان المدعي يدعي ،ألفين وعلى هذا المائة والمائتان والطلقة والطلقتان والطلقة والثلاث؛ كذا في الكافي. وقد أشار بتفسير الموافقة إلى أنه لا يشترط أن يكون بعين ذلك اللفظ بل إما بعينه أو بمرادفه حتى لو شهد أحدهما بالهبة والآخر بالعطية تقبل، وبه اندفع ما في النهاية أن المطابقة في المعنى كافية للفرع المذكور لحصول المطابقة لفظاً ما لو شهد أحدهما بأنه قال لها أنت خلية وشهد الآخر بأنه قال لها أنت برية حيث لا تقبل لأنهما لفظان متباينان وإن اشتركا في لازم واحد وهو البينونة لأن معنى خلية غير معنى برية، وعلى هذا لو شهد أحدهما بالنكاح والآخر بالتزويج فإنها تقبل كما في المحيط. ولو شهد أحدهما بالغصب أو القتل والآخر بالإقرار به لا تقبل؛ ذكره الشارح . وفي العمدة: قوله: (فغير متصور شرعاً قال الرملي أقول قال الغزي ممنوع لأنه لو ادعى أنه ملكي وأنه أقر له به تسمع لكن قد يقال رجع إلى دعوى الملك والكلام ليس فيه فيستقيم كلامه رحمه الله تعالى قوله : (و به اندفع ما في النهاية الخ) لا يخفى أن ما في النهاية هو عين ما قرره من أ أن الشرط تطابق اللفظين على إفادة المعنى وأنه لا يشترط أن يكون بعين ذلك اللفظ بل به أو بمرادفه وهذا معنى قوله إن المطابقة في المعنى كافية ومراده المطابقة بطريق الوضع لا التضمن بدليل قوله في النهاية «المقصود ما تضمنه اللفظ وهو ما صار اللفظ علماً عليه فإن ما صار اللفظ علماً عليه هو معناه المطابقي كما لا يخفى فتدبر قوله ولو) شهد أحدهما بالغصب أو القتل والآخر بالإقرار به لا تقبل الخ) قال
His statement: 'And agreement of the two witnesses in wording and meaning is required' means according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him. According to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], agreement in meaning is sufficient. What is meant by their agreement in wording is that their two utterances correspond in conveying the meaning by way of proper signification (al-wad'), not by way of implication. So if someone claims against another one hundred dirhams, and one witness testifies to one dirham, another to two dirhams, another to three, another to four, and another to five, according to Abu Hanifa none is accepted due to lack of verbal agreement. According to the two, the judgment is for four dirhams. Similarly, if one testifies to a thousand and another to two thousand, according to him it is not accepted, and according to the two it is accepted for one thousand if the claimant claims two thousand. And likewise for one hundred and two hundred, and for one divorce and two divorces, and one divorce and three; as in al-Kafi. And he indicated by his interpretation of agreement that it is not required to be the exact same word, but either the same or its synonym, so that if one testifies to a gift (hiba) and the other to a gift (atiyya), it is accepted. And by this, what is in al-Nihaya is refuted: that agreement in meaning is sufficient for the mentioned branch—because verbal agreement occurs when one testifies that he said to her 'you are khaliyya' and the other testifies that he said 'you are barriyya,' which is not accepted because they are two different words even though they share one necessary implication, which is separation, because the meaning of khaliyya is not the same as the meaning of barriyya. Based on this, if one testifies to marriage (nikah) and the other to marriage (tazwij), it is accepted as in al-Muhit. If one testifies to usurpation or murder and the other to a confession of that, it is not accepted; the commentator mentioned it. And in al-Umda: His statement: 'so it is not legally conceivable' - al-Ramli said, 'I say,' al-Ghazzi said, 'It is not allowed, because if he claims that it is my property and that he confessed it to me, it is heard, but it may be said that it reverts to a claim of ownership, and the discussion is not about that, so his statement is correct, may Allah have mercy on him.' His statement: 'And by this what is in al-Nihaya is refuted...' - it is clear that what is in al-Nihaya is exactly what he established: that the condition is that the two utterances correspond in conveying the meaning, and it is not required to be the exact same word but either it or its synonym. This is the meaning of his statement that agreement in meaning is sufficient, and he means agreement by way of proper signification (al-wad'), not by way of implication. The evidence is his statement in al-Nihaya: 'What is intended is what the word implies, and that is what the word is a sign for; what the word is a sign for is its proper meaning (ma'na mutabaqi), as is obvious. So ponder. His statement: 'If one testifies to usurpation or murder and the other to a confession of that, it is not accepted.'
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn statement: 'And agreement of the two witnesses in wording and meaning is required.' It opens with an intra-Hanafi dispute: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, witnesses must agree in both wording and meaning; according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad), agreement in meaning alone suffices. The key concept is that 'agreement in wording' means the two utterances correspond in conveying the meaning by way of proper signification (wad'), not by way of implication (tadammun). This is illustrated with examples: if witnesses testify to different amounts (e.g., one says 1 dirham, another says 2 dirhams), Abu Hanifa rejects all testimony due to lack of verbal agreement, while the Sahibayn accept the lowest common amount (4 dirhams in the example with multiple witnesses). The commentator then clarifies that the requirement is not for exact same words—synonyms are acceptable, such as 'hiba' and 'atiya' (both meaning gift). This principle refutes a misunderstanding from al-Nihaya, which might suggest that mere agreement in meaning is sufficient even if words are not synonyms. The passage then gives specific examples: 'khaliyya' and 'barriyya' (both terms for divorce) are not acceptable because they are different words with different literal meanings, even though they both imply separation. Conversely, 'nikah' and 'tazwij' (marriage) are synonyms, so testimony is accepted. Finally, if one witness testifies to a substantive act (usurpation/murder) and the other to a confession of that act, the testimony is not accepted because the subject matter differs (substantive vs. evidentiary). The commentary then engages with additional points from al-Umda about the conceivability of a claim of confession and refines the understanding of agreement.

Key Terms
اتفاق الشاهدين (ittifaq al-shahidayn): The condition that two witnesses must concur in their testimony, both in wording and meaning, for it to be accepted.
وضع (wad'): The literal or proper signification of a word as assigned by language, as opposed to implied or necessary meaning.
تضمن (tadammun): Implication; a meaning that is necessarily implied by the literal meaning but not directly stated.
مرادف (muradif): Synonym; a word that shares the same literal meaning as another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if one witness testifies that the defendant said 'you are khaliyya' and the other testifies that he said 'you are barriyya', what is the ruling?
A) The testimony is accepted because both imply divorce (baynuna).
B) The testimony is not accepted because the words are not synonyms and have different proper meanings.
C) The testimony is accepted only if it is for a living person.
D) The testimony is accepted if the claimant does not object.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi condition for witness testimony requires agreement in literal or synonymous wording, not just implied meaning.

Acceptance of Testimony with Varied Agency Terms
Rulings on testimony when witnesses differ in wording for agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that testimony regarding an agency appointment is accepted despite differences in wording, as long as the essential meaning of authorization is preserved.

Core Idea
Testimony on agency is valid if the meaning is clear, even if terms differ.

This passage from Munyat al-Mufti and Adab al-Quda presents a series of cases where witnesses describe an agency appointment using different verbs and phrases. The common thread is that the Hanafi school accepts the testimony as long as the core fact—that the principal authorized the agent to collect or demand—is unequivocal. These rulings illustrate a broader principle: legal validity does not depend on exact wording when the intended meaning is apparent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common element in all cases
Each case involves two witnesses who describe the agency differently. List the verbs used: wakkala, jarra, sallata, awsa, amara, arsala. Note that all imply authorization to collect or demand a debt.
The specific action (qabd, taqadi, talab) may vary, but the overall authorization is consistent.
2
Determine the legal significance of the difference
In each pair, the difference is about the specific term, but the action (authorizing collection/demand) remains the same. Ask: does the difference change the legal effect? No.
The witnesses agree on the substance, not the wording.
3
Extract the Hanafi principle
The testimony is accepted because the essential meaning (al-ma'na) is consistent. The Hanafi school prioritizes substance over form in this context.
This principle is applied consistently across all eight cases.
4
Consider exception for differing locations
Case 32 shows that even if witnesses differ on the judge or location (Kufa vs. Basra), the testimony is still accepted because the agency itself is not defined by location.
The location is an ancillary detail, not a core element of the agency.
5
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
If one witness says 'agent for receipt' and another says 'agent to take delivery', both indicate permission to take possession. The testimony would be accepted.
Always check whether the witnesses agree on the same underlying authorization.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثانية والثلاثون من وكالة منية المفتي شهد واحد أنه وكله بالخصومة في هذه الدار عند قاضي الكوفة وآخر قال عند قاضي البصرة جازت شهادتهما ا هـ. الثالثة والثلاثون في أدب القضاء للخصاف من باب الشهادة بالوكالة شهد أحدهما أنه وكله بالقبض والآخر أنه جراه تقبل الرابعة والثلاثون شهد أحدهما أنه وكله بقبضه والآخر أنه سلطه على قبضه تقبل الخامسة والثلاثون شهد أحدهما أنه وكله بقبضه والآخر أنه أوصى إليه بقبضه في حياته تقبل السادسة والثلاثون شهد أحدهما أنه وكله بطلب دينه والآخر بتقاضيه تقبل. السابعة والثلاثون شهد أحدهما أنه وكله بقبضه والآخر بتقاضيه أو طلبه تقبل. الثامنة والثلاثون شهد أحدهما أنه وكله بقبضه والآخر أنه أمره بأخده أو أرسله ليأخذه تقبل ا هـ . وهي في أدب القضاء وما قبلها
The thirty-second: From Wakalah of Munyat al-Mufti: One witness testified that he appointed him as agent for litigation in this house before the judge of Kufa, and another said before the judge of Basra; their testimony is permissible. The thirty-third: In Adab al-Quda of al-Khassaf, from the chapter of testimony on agency: One testified that he appointed him as agent for receipt (qabd), and the other that he made him a jari (one who collects); it is accepted. The thirty-fourth: One testified that he appointed him as agent for receipt, and the other that he gave him power (sallatahu) over receipt; it is accepted. The thirty-fifth: One testified that he appointed him as agent for receipt, and the other that he appointed him as executor (awsa ilayhi) for receipt during his lifetime; it is accepted. The thirty-sixth: One testified that he appointed him as agent to demand his debt, and the other to claim it (taqadi); it is accepted. The thirty-seventh: One testified that he appointed him as agent for receipt, and the other to claim or demand it; it is accepted. The thirty-eighth: One testified that he appointed him as agent for receipt, and the other that he ordered him to take it or sent him to take it; it is accepted. All are from Adab al-Quda and earlier.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This is a series of rulings (32-38) all about agency testimony where witnesses use different wording to describe the agency. The common principle is that as long as they agree on the essential fact of being authorized to collect or demand a debt, the testimony is accepted even if they use different terms (e.g., 'appointed as agent', 'made him a jari', 'gave him power', 'appointed as executor', 'ordered him', 'sent him'). The Hanafi school is lenient here because the meaning is the same. Issue 32 specifically addresses the location/judge: even if they differ on which judge's court the agency was for, it is accepted because the agency itself is the same.

Key Terms
جَرَاهُ (jarah): A term meaning he made him a 'jari', i.e., an agent for collection.
سَلَّطَهُ (sallatahu): He gave him power or authority over something.
أَوْصَى إِلَيْهِ (awsa ilayhi): He appointed him as executor or trustee (wasi) for a task.
تَقَاضَى (taqada): To claim or demand payment of a debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If one witness says the defendant appointed the plaintiff as agent for receipt (وكله بقبضه), and another says he gave him power over receipt (سلطه على قبضه), is the testimony accepted?
A) No, because the terms differ
B) Yes, because the meaning is the same
C) No, unless the terms are identical
D) Yes, but only if the plaintiff is an agent

Key Takeaway
Testimony on agency is accepted as long as the witnesses agree on the essential authorization, regardless of the precise wording.

Liability Upon Retraction of Branch and Original Witnesses
Rulings on liability when branch and original witnesses retract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the liability rules for retracting branch and original witnesses, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute, and apply the fractions used in partial retractions.

Core Idea
Branch witnesses are liable; original witnesses are not if they deny the appointment.

In Hanafi law, when witnesses retract after a judgment, the question of liability arises. This lesson examines the distinction between branch witnesses (who testify based on others' testimony) and original witnesses (who have direct knowledge). The central ruling from the matn states that branch witnesses are liable, while original witnesses are not if they deny having appointed the branch. We will unpack the reasoning, explore the internal Hanafi difference, and see how liability is divided among multiple groups of witnesses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the matn statement: branch witnesses are liable upon retraction; original witnesses are not if they say 'We did not appoint the branch' or 'We erred.' Note the immediate consequence: liability is wajib on the branch.
This is the default position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Determine how Muhammad differs: he holds original witnesses liable because the branch transmitted their testimony. Contrast this with the majority view that the judgment rests on the branch's own testimony.
The proof: the judge rules on what he observes in court (the branch's testimony).
3
Examine the fractions in al-Muhit and al-Jami'
When multiple groups of branch witnesses retract, the liability is divided proportionally. Study the examples: two groups testifying on testimony of four and two, or on two and one. Note the difference between Abu Yusuf (two-thirds/one-third) and Muhammad (half/half).
These fractions apply when the total liability is fixed (e.g., 1000 dirhams).
4
Distinguish qiyas vs. istihsan
The commentator notes that al-Mabsut's answer (half/half) is based on qiyas, while al-Jami's various fractions are based on istihsan. Understand that istihsan yields different proportions based on the number of witnesses and their roles.
The relied-upon position is the istihsan from al-Jami'.
5
Apply the principle to waqf and other cases
The passage extends to a scenario where witnesses testify that someone is a beneficiary of a waqf. If they retract, they are not liable for future produce (ghallah) but are liable for produce that existed at the time of testimony and was consumed.
The illa: the loss (itlaf) must be actual at the time of testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نشهد الفروع على شهادتنا أو أشهدناهم وغلطنا ولو رجع الأصول والفروع ضمن مع يمينه لإنكاره الزيادة، فإن برهن الطالب وقضى ثم رجعا ضمنا الخمسمائة الواجبة بشهادتهما، وفيه دليل على أن الجواب في المسألة الأولى سهو حيث أجابوا بعدم الضمان . شهدا على العفو عن دم فيه مال أو جرح عمد فيه مال ثم رجعا ضمنا الدية وأرش الجراحة في ثلاث سنين أو سنة .اهـ. وفي البدائع : شهدا بالقتل خطأ ثم رجعا ضمنا الدية في مالهما، وكذا إذا شهدا بقطع يد خطأ ضمنا نصفها وكذا إذا شهدا بسرقة فقطع ثم رجعا اهـ. وفي السراج الوهاج أن الدية التي على الشاهدين تكون في مالهما في ثلاث سنين ولا كفارة عليهما ولا يحرمان الميراث بأن كانا ولدي المشهود عليه فإنهما يرثانه اهـ قوله : (وإن رجع شهود الفرع ضمنوا لأن الشهادة في مجلس القضاء صدرت منهم فكان التلف مضافاً إليهم. وفي المحيط : شهدا على شهادة أربعة وآخران على شهادة شاهدين وقضى ثم رجعوا فعلى شاهدي الأربعة ثلثا الضمان وعلى الآخرين الثلث عند أبي يوسف. وقال محمد: على الفريقين نصفان. الجامع : شهدا على شهادة شاهدين لرجل على آخر بألف وشهد آخران على شهادة واحد عليه بألف فقضى بشهادتهم ثم رجع أحد اللذين شهدا على شهادة الشاهدين وأحد اللذين شهدا على شهادة واحد فعليهما ثلاثة أثمان الحق ثمنان على الأول وثمن على الآخر، ولو لم يرجع إلا واحد من الفريق الأول ضمن الربع ، ولو رجع بعد هذا الفريق الآخر كلهم ضمنا ربعاً آخر، ولو شهد كل فريق على شهادة شاهدين ورجع واحد من هذا وواحد من ذلك ضمنا ثمنين ونصفاً. وذكر في المبسوط النصف، وعن الكرخي يضمنان الربع، وعن عيسى بن أبان الثلث، والأصح أن المذكور في المبسوط جواب القياس، والمذكور في الجامع جواب الاستحسان اهـ. قوله : (لا شهود الأصل بلم نشهد الفروع على شهادتنا أو أشهدناهم وغلطنا) أي لا ضمان عليهم فيهما؛ أما في الأولى فلأنهم أنكروا السبب وهو الإشهاد فلا يبطل القضاء لأنه خبر محتمل فصار كرجوع الشاهد بخلاف ما قبل القضاء، وأما في الثانية فهو قولهما. وقال محمد: يضمنون لأن الفروع نقلوا شهادة الأصول فصار كأنهم حضروا. ولهما أن القضاء وقع بشهادة الفروع لأن القاضي يقضي بما يعاين من الحجة وهي شهادتهم، وقدمنا أنه يؤخذ من هذه المسألة أنهما لو شهدا بأنه من مستحقي هذا الوقف فقضى القاضي به بشهادتهما ثم رجعا لا يضمنان شيئاً للمشهود عليهم من الغلة فيما يستقبل لأنهما لم يتلفاها عليهم لعدم وجودها وقتئذ حتى لو كان شيء من الغلة موجوداً وقت الشهادة وحكم به يضمنان بالرجوع ما أخذه الشهود له أو استهلك المشهود عليهم غلة السنين الماضية وحكم عليهم له بها، فكذلك يضمنانها لأنهما أتلفاه على المشهود عليهم بشهادتهما كمسألة الشهادة بعد موت المولى هنا ولم أر من صرح بذلك وقد سئلت عنه فاستخرجت الجواب من مسألة البدائع المذكورة فتأمل ذلك الخ.
We testify that the branch (witnesses testified) based on our testimony, or we appointed them and we erred. And if both the original and branch witnesses retract, they are liable together with his oath due to his denial of the excess. If the claimant provides proof and the judge gives judgment, then they retract, they guarantee the five hundred that were wajib by their testimony. In this is evidence that the answer in the first issue was an oversight where they answered with no liability. They testified about pardon for blood in which there is property or intentional wound in which there is property, then they retract; they guarantee the diyah and the 'arsh of the wound over three years or one year. End. In al-Bada'i': They testified about killing by mistake (khata') and then retracted; they guarantee the diyah from their own wealth. Similarly, if they testified about cutting off a hand by mistake, they guarantee half of it. Similarly, if they testified about theft and (the hand) was cut, then they retract. End. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: The diyah that is upon the two witnesses is from their wealth over three years, and there is no expiation upon them, nor are they deprived of inheritance; if they are sons of the person testified against, they inherit from him. End. His statement: (And if the branch witnesses retract, they are liable) because the testimony was given by them in the court, so the loss is attributed to them. In al-Muhit: They testified regarding the testimony of four (witnesses), and two others regarding the testimony of two witnesses, and judgment was given, then they retract. According to Abu Yusuf, upon the two witnesses of four is two-thirds of the liability, and upon the other two is one-third. Muhammad said: Upon the two groups, half each. In al-Jami': They testified regarding the testimony of two witnesses for a man against another for a thousand, and two others testified regarding the testimony of one against him for a thousand, and judgment was given based on their testimony, then one of those who testified regarding the testimony of the two witnesses retracted and one of those who testified regarding the testimony of the one retracted; upon them is three-eighths of the right: two-eighths upon the first and one-eighth upon the other. If only one from the first group retracted, he guarantees one quarter. If after that all of the other group retract, they guarantee another quarter. If each group testified regarding the testimony of two witnesses and one from this and one from that retracted, they guarantee two and a half eighths. Al-Mabsut mentions the half, from al-Karkhi they guarantee the quarter, from 'Isa ibn Aban the third. The most correct is that mentioned in al-Mabsut is the answer of qiyas, and mentioned in al-Jami' is the answer of istihsan. End. His statement: (Not the original witnesses, but we testify that the branch (testified) based on our testimony or we appointed them and we erred) i.e., no liability upon them in both cases. As for the first, because they denied the cause (sabab), which is the appointment (ishhad), so the judgment is not invalidated because it is a probable report, thus it becomes like the retraction of a witness, unlike before judgment. As for the second, it is their statement. Muhammad said: They are liable because the branch transmitted the testimony of the original, so it is as if they attended. According to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the judgment was based on the testimony of the branch because the judge judges by what he observes as evidence, which is their testimony. And we have already stated that from this issue, it is derived that if they testify that someone is among the beneficiaries of this waqf, and the judge gives judgment based on their testimony, then they retract, they are not liable for anything to those testified against from future produce (ghallah) because they did not cause its loss as it did not exist at that time. But if some produce existed at the time of testimony and judgment was given, they become liable upon retraction for what the beneficiary took or what was consumed by those testified against from past years' produce that was adjudged to him, so they likewise guarantee it because they caused its loss through their testimony, like the issue of testimony after the death of the master here. I have not seen anyone explicitly stating this, and I was asked about it, so I extracted the answer from the mentioned issue in al-Bada'i'. So ponder that. End.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage deals with the retraction of branch witnesses (shuhud al-far') and original witnesses (shuhud al-asl). The matn states that if branch witnesses retract, they are liable; original witnesses are not liable if they say 'We testify that the branch (testified) based on our testimony or we appointed them and we erred.' The commentary explains the reasoning: the branch witnesses' testimony was the basis of the judgment, so the loss is attributed to them. For original witnesses, if they deny the cause (the appointment), the judgment remains, as their statement is a probable report. Imam Muhammad differs, holding them liable because the branch transmitted their testimony. The dominant view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that the judge rules on the branch's testimony directly. The passage also includes detailed calculations from al-Muhit and al-Jami' on how liability is divided among multiple groups of witnesses when they retract. According to Abu Yusuf, the group that testified on the testimony of four witnesses bears two-thirds, while the group on the testimony of two bears one-third. Muhammad holds half each. Further sub-cases involve partial retractions. The commentator notes that the answer based on qiyas is in al-Mabsut (half), while the answer based on istihsan is in al-Jami' (various fractions). The passage concludes with an application to waqf: witnesses who testify that someone is a beneficiary and then retract are not liable for future produce (since it didn't exist), but if produce existed at the time of testimony and was adjudged, they are liable for what was taken or consumed.

Key Terms
شهود الأصل (shuhud al-asl): Original witnesses who have direct knowledge and whose testimony is transmitted by branch witnesses
شهود الفرع (shuhud al-far'): Branch witnesses who testify based on the testimony of the original witnesses
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference, a method of departing from qiyas in favor of a more equitable ruling

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, are original witnesses liable if they retract by saying 'We did not appoint the branch'?
A) Yes, they are liable
B) No, they are not liable
C) Only if the branch also retracts
D) They are liable but can seek recourse

Key Takeaway
Branch witnesses bear liability upon retraction because their testimony directly caused the judgment; original witnesses are not liable if they deny the appointment, as per the majority Hanafi view.

The Definition and Pillar of Legal Agency (Wakala)
Defines wakala linguistically and technically, and states its pillar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and technical definitions of wakala and identify its pillar (rukn) as offer and acceptance, including implicit acceptance.

Core Idea
Agency is appointing another for a known disposition; its pillar is offer and acceptance, even if implied.

This lesson opens the Book of Agency in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. Before we can apply the rules of agency, we must precisely understand what wakala is and what constitutes its essential element (rukn). The author defines wakala linguistically as delegation, and technically as placing another in one's stead for a known action. He then states that the pillar of agency is the offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul), which can be explicit or implied by context.

Guided Path
1
Linguistic Definition
Understand that wakala linguistically means tawkil (delegation) and is derived from the root w-k-l. Note the lexical meaning: putting another in charge.
The passage cites al-Misbah to confirm this.
2
Technical Definition
The passage states: 'إقامة الإنسان غيره مقام نفسه في تصرف معلوم' – appointing another in one's place for a known disposition. This is the core Hanafi definition.
Remember the qualification 'known disposition'.
3
Identify the Rukn
The pillar is 'ما دل عليها من الإيجاب والقبول ولو حكما' – what indicates it: offer and acceptance, even if implicit. Understand that implicit acceptance can be inferred from context.
Implicit acceptance (hukman) is sufficient.
4
Scope Qualification
The phrase 'في تصرف معلوم' limits agency to specified actions. General agency is possible, but the disposition must be known or determinable.
This prevents open-ended authorization.
5
Application to Examples
The passage gives an example: if the agent acts beyond the scope, it is not binding on the principal unless there was prior conversation. This illustrates the importance of defining the scope.
The example of the agent who divorces or frees slaves without authority.

Source Text

Book of Agency. Authorization is valid, and it is appointing another in one's place in a disposition that one has the right to perform, provided the agent is... Book of Agency. Commentary
This passage introduces the Book of Agency (Kitab al-Wakala) from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. It begins by defining wakala linguistically (meaning tawkil, delegation) and technically (appointing another in one's place for a known disposition). The author then discusses the pillar (rukn) of agency, which is offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul), even if implied (hukman). It provides an example: if the principal says 'I appoint you as agent in this,' the agent is only authorized for preservation (the minimum). If the agent goes beyond the scope of the authorization, the principal may not be bound. The passage also notes that if the principal and agent have a prior understanding, the agent's actions within that understanding are binding. This is foundational for understanding the contract of agency in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
الوكالة (al-wakala): Linguistically, delegation of a disposition to another; technically, appointing another in one's place for a known disposition.
التوكيل (al-tawkil): The act of appointing an agent; the same as wakala linguistically.
الإيجاب والقبول (al-ijab wa al-qabul): Offer and acceptance; the two components of the pillar (rukn) of agency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Written contract
B) Offer and acceptance (explicit or implicit)
C) Presence of witnesses
D) Payment of fee

Key Takeaway
Wakala is valid when one person delegates a known disposition to another through offer and acceptance, which can be explicit or implied.

Definition and Pillar of Wikalah (Agency)
Defines wikalah linguistically and technically, and explains its pillar (ijab and qabul) including implicit acceptance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of wikalah (agency) and identify its pillar (rukn) with examples of express and implied acceptance.

Core Idea
Agency is valid by offer and acceptance, even implied — the scope must be known to avoid ambiguity.

This lesson opens the Book of Agency from al-Bahr al-Raiq. We will examine the linguistic and technical definitions of wikalah, then focus on its essential pillar: ijab and qabul, including cases where silence suffices. Understanding this foundation is critical because the scope of authority must be clear, and any act outside it does not bind the principal.

Guided Path
1
Trace the linguistic root
Look at the passage's linguistic analysis from al-Misbah. Note the dual meaning of wakil: delegated to (maf'ul) and protector (fa'il). Understand that wikalah means tawkil (entrusting).
The Qur'anic verse 'Hasbuna Allah wa ni'ma al-wakil' uses wakil in the sense of Protector.
2
Extract the technical definition
Find the phrase 'إقامة الإنسان غيره مقام نفسه في تصرف معلوم' and note the key condition: the disposition (tasarruf) must be known (ma'lum). Why is this condition important?
This condition distinguishes agency from general delegation, preventing gharar.
3
Identify the rukn
The passage states the pillar is 'ما دل عليها من الإيجاب والقبول ولو حكما' — offer and acceptance, even if implied (hukman). What does 'hukman' mean in this context?
Implied acceptance can be by conduct or silence when there is evidence of consent.
4
Apply to a scenario
Consider the example: principal says 'I appoint you agent in this.' The agent is authorized only for custody (hifz). If the agent performs a different act, it is not binding. Analyze why the scope is interpreted minimally.
The principle of 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' applies: the agent's authority is limited to what is clearly intended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوكالة صح التوكيل وهو إقامة الغير مقام نفسه في التصرف ممن يملكه إذا كان الوكيل : كتاب الوكالة مناسبتها ا من حيث إن الانسان يحتاج في معاشه إلى التعاضد والشهادة منه فكذا الوكالة. والكلام فيها في مواضع الأول في معناها لغة قال في المصباح : وكلت إليه الأمر وكلاً من باب وعد، ووكولاً فوضته إليه واكتفيت به الوکیل فعيل بمعنى مفعول لأنه موكول إليه، ويكون بمعنى فاعل إذا كان بمعنى الحافظ ومنه حسبنا الله ونعم الوكيل والجمع وكلاء. ووكلته توكيلاً فتوكيل قبل الوكالة وهي بفتح الواو والكسر لغة، وتوكل على الله تعالى اعتمد عليه ا هـ . والحاصل أنها في اللغة بمعنى التوكيل وهو تفويض التصرف إلى الغير . الثاني في معناها اصطلاحاً فهي : إقامة الإنسان غيره مقام نفسه في تصرف معلوم ؛ كذا في العناية : الثالث في ركنها وهو ما دل عليها من الإيجاب والقبول ولو حكماً فلو قال وكلتك في هذا كان وكيلاً بحفظه لأنه الأدنى فيحمل عليه ؛ هكذا ذكروا . وقيدوا بقوله في هذا لأنه لو قال وكلتك فقال قبلت الوكالة فقال الوكيل طلقت امرأتك ثلاثاً أو أعتقت عبدك فلاناً أو زوجت بنتك فلانة من فلان أو تصدقت من مالك بكذا على الفقراء فقال الرجل لا أرضى بذلك فهذا الكلام متوجه إلى الذي تحاورا فيه وقليلاً ما يكون هذا الكلام والتفويض الأبناء على سابقة تجري بينهما، فإن كان كذلك فالأمر على ما تعارفوه بما جرت المخاطبة فيه، فإن فعل شيئاً خارجاً من ذلك النوع لم ينفذ على الموكل دون كتاب الوكالة قوله: (ولو حكما دخل به السكوت كما سننبه عليه قبيل الرابع وسيأتي في الفصل الآتي في إنفاذه؛ كذا في خزانة المفتين.
Book of Agency. The authorization is valid, and it is the replacement of another in one's place in a disposition from someone who owns it, if the agent is... Book of Agency. Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq opens the Book of Agency (Kitab al-Wikalah) by defining the term and establishing its essential pillar. The commentator begins with the matn statement that authorization (tawkil) is valid, meaning the act of appointing another to act on one's behalf. He then explains the rationale: humans need mutual assistance, and agency facilitates trade and legal transactions. The discussion is structured into three topics. First, the linguistic meaning: drawing from al-Misbah, he explains that 'wakala ilayhi al-amr' means to delegate the affair, and 'wakil' is the one delegated to, also meaning protector as in the Qur'anic phrase 'Hasbuna Allah wa ni'ma al-wakil.' Second, the technical definition from al-Inayah: agency is the replacement of another in one's place in a known disposition (tasarruf ma'lum). This emphasizes that the scope must be known to avoid ambiguity. Third, the pillar (rukn) of agency is the offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul), even if implied (hukman). The commentator provides an example: if the principal says 'I appoint you agent in this,' the agent is authorized only for custody (hifz) because that is the minimal action. But if the wording is absolute, the scope depends on the parties' common understanding. If the agent performs an act outside that understood scope, it does not bind the principal. The passage ends by noting that silence can constitute acceptance, as will be elaborated later. This foundation is crucial because the Hanafi school distinguishes agency as a contract requiring mutual consent, and the exact scope of authority must be determinable either explicitly or by custom.

Key Terms
الوكالة (al-wikalah): Appointing another to act on one's behalf in a legal disposition
التوكيل (al-tawkil): The act of delegating authority to an agent
الركن (al-rukn): The essential component of a contract without which it is invalid; here, ijab and qabul
الإيجاب (al-ijab): The offer made by the principal indicating his intention to appoint an agent
القبول (al-qabul): The acceptance by the agent, which may be by words or conduct indicating consent

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) A written contract with witnesses.
B) Offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul), even if implied.
C) Delivery of a fee to the agent.
D) The presence of a judge.

Key Takeaway
The validity of agency hinges on offer and acceptance (even implied), and the scope of the agent's authority must be clearly defined to avoid binding the principal beyond intent.

Scope of Agency Based on Different Wordings
Compilation of rulings on agent's permissible actions based on appointment wording

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the scope of an agent's authority by analyzing the wording of the appointment and applying Hanafi default interpretations.

Core Idea
An agent's authority is limited to what is explicitly stated; general wording defaults to custody (hifz) by istihsan.

The Hanafi school places great emphasis on the precise wording used when appointing an agent, as different phrases confer different scopes of authority. This lesson examines numerous scenarios from al-Bahr al-Raiq, showing how the principal's words determine whether the agent can sell, buy, collect debts, manage property, or even divorce. Understanding these nuances is critical to avoid invalid actions and to correctly delegate powers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wording used by the principal
Look at the exact phrase, e.g., 'You are my agent in everything,' 'I permit you to sell,' 'I delegated to you the matter of my debts.' Note whether it is general, specific, or conditional.
The passage lists many wordings; each triggers a different scope.
2
Classify the type of delegation
Determine if the wording implies a general grant (tafwid), a specific mandate (tawkil), or something in between. A general grant without qualification defaults to custody (hifz) by istihsan, despite qiyas suggesting voidness due to ignorance.
3
Apply the default interpretation
For ambiguous phrases like 'in everything,' the Hanafi school uses istihsan to restrict scope to custody unless additional words expand it. For specific assets (debts, animals, wife), the default scope is defined by custom and need.
Custody includes preservation but not sale, purchase, or gift unless explicitly added.
4
Check for expansions or restrictions
If the principal adds 'your command is permissible' or similar, the scope expands to sale, purchase, gift, and charity, but according to Abu Hanifa, not to emancipation or gratuitous transfers (the fatwa is on this restriction).
5
Identify the thamarah (practical consequence)
The ruling determines whether the agent's action is valid. For example, an agent authorized only for custody who sells the principal's property acts without authority; the sale is void unless ratified. Conversely, an agent with expanded powers must act within the limits of the wording.
This step is crucial for applying the rulings in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال أنت وكيلي في كل شيء كان تفويضاً للحفظ، والقياس أن لا يكون وكيلاً به للجهالة، والاستحسان انصرافها إلى الحفظ، ولو قال أجزت لك بيع هذا عبدي أنه يكون توكيلاً بالبيع ولو زاد على قوله أنت وكيلي في كل شيء جائز أمرك ملك الحفظ والبيع والشراء ويملك الهبة والصدقة حتى إذا أنفق على نفسه من ذلك المال جاز حتى يعلم خلافه من قصد الموكل . وعن الإمام تخصيصه بالمعاوضات ولا يلي العتق والتبرع وعليه الفتوى، وكذا إذا قال طلقت امرأتك ووقفت ووهبت أرضك في الأصح لا يجوز . وفي الروضة : فوضت أمري إليك قيل هذا باطل، وقيل هذا والأول سواء في أنه تفويض الحفظ. ولو قال مالك المستغلات فوضت إليك أمر مستغلاتي وكان أجرها من إنسان ملك تقاضى الأجرة وقبضها، وكذا لو قال إليك أمر ديوني ملك التقاضي، ولو قال إليك فوضت أمر دوابي وأمر مماليكي ملك الحفظ والرعي والتعليف والنفقة عليهم . فوضت إليك أمر امرأتي ملك طلاقها واقتصر على المجلس بخلاف قوله ملكتك حيث لا يقتصر على المجلس ؛ كذا في البزازية . وفي كافي الحاكم . لو وكله بالقيام على داره وإجارتها وقبض غلتها والبيع لم يكن له أن يبني ولا أن يرم منها شيئاً وليس وكيلاً في خصومتها، ولو هدم رجل منها شيئاً كان وكيلاً في الخصومة لأنه استهلك شيئاً في يديه، وكذا لو أجرها من رجل فجحد ذلك الرجل الإجارة كان خصماً فيها حتى يثبتها ، وكذا إذا سكنها وجحد وقال في باب الوكالة بالدين : لو وكله بتقاضي كل دين له ثم حدث له دين بعد ذلك الأجرا هـ. فهو وكيل في قبضه، ولو وكله بقبض غلة أرضه وثمرتها كان له أن يقبض ذلك كل سنة ا هـ . وقال في باب قبض الوديعة والعارية : ولو وكله بقبض عبد عند رجل فقتل العبد خطأ كان للمودع أن يأخذ القيمة من عاقلة القاتل وليس للوكيل أن يقبض القيمة لأنها كالثمن، ولو كان الوكيل قبض العبد فقتل عنده كان له أن يأخذ القيمة وهو الآن بمنزلة الأول، ولو جنى على العبد جناية قبل أن يقبضه الوكيل فأخذ المستودع أرشها فللوكيل أن يقبض العبد دون الأرش، وكذا لو كان المستودع آجره بإذن مولاه لم يأخذ الوكيل أجره، وكذا مهر الأمة إذا وطئت بشبهة . ولو وكله بقبض أمة أو شاة فولدت كان للوكيل أن يقبض الولد مع الأم ، ولو كانت ولدت قبل أن يوكله بقبضها لم يكن له أن يقبض الولد، وكذلك ثمرة البستان بمنزلة الولدا وفي البدائع : وأما ركن التوكيل فهو الإيجاب والقبول ؛ فالإيجاب من الموكل أن يقول وكلتك بكذا أو افعل كذا أو أذنت لك أن تفعل كذا ونحوه . والقبول من الوكيل أن يقول قبلت وما يجري مجراه فما لم يوجد لم يتم، ولهذا لو وكل إنساناً بقبض دينه فأبى أن يقبض ثم ذهب فقبض لم يبرأ الغريم لأنه ارتد بالرد. ثم الركن قد يكون مطلقاً وقد يكون معلقاً بشرط نحو إن قدم زيد فأنت وكيلي في بيع هذا هـ. شرح قوله ولو وكله بشراء شيء بعينه لا يشتريه لنفسه عن الرملي التفرقة في الحكم بين القبول الصريح وبين السكوت فراجعه .
If he says: 'You are my agent in everything,' it is a delegation of custody. By analogy he would not be an agent due to ignorance, but by istihsan it is turned to custody. If he says: 'I permitted you to sell this slave of mine,' it is an agency for sale. If he adds to his saying 'You are my agent in everything' or 'your command is permissible,' he owns custody, sale, purchase, and he owns gift and charity, so that if he spends from that wealth on himself, it is permissible until he knows otherwise from the intention of the principal. From Imam Abu Hanifa: it is restricted to commutative transactions, and he is not authorized for emancipation and gratuitous transfers, and upon this is the fatwa. Similarly, if he says 'I divorced your wife, and I endowed and gifted your land,' in the most correct view it is not permissible. In al-Rawdah: 'I delegated my matter to you' – it is said this is void, and it is said this and the first are the same in that it is a delegation of custody. If someone of possessing income properties says: 'I delegated to you the matter of my income properties,' and its rent was from a person, he owns the right to demand the rent and receive it. Similarly, if he says 'To you is the matter of my debts,' he owns the right to demand payment. If he says 'I delegated to you the matter of my animals and my slaves,' he owns custody, grazing, feeding, and spending on them. 'I delegated to you the matter of my wife,' he owns her divorce and is restricted to the session, unlike his saying 'I gave you possession' where there is no restriction to the session; as in al-Bazzaziyya. In Kafi al-Hakim: If he authorizes him to manage his house, rent it out, receive its produce, and sell, he does not have the right to build or repair anything from it, and he is not an agent for litigation about it. If a man demolishes something from it, he becomes an agent for litigation because he consumed something in his hands. Similarly, if he rents it to a man and that man denies the lease, he is a litigant for it until he proves it. Similarly, if he lives in it and denies. He said in the chapter of Agency for Debt: If he authorizes him to receive every debt of his, then a debt occurs after that (the authorization), he is an agent for its receipt. If he authorizes him to receive the produce of his land and its fruits, he may receive that every year. End. He said in the chapter of Receipt of Deposit and Loan: If he authorizes him to receive a slave from a man, and the slave is killed accidentally, the depositor may take the blood money from the 'aqila of the killer, and the agent does not have the right to receive the blood money because it is like a price. If the agent had received the slave and then the slave was killed in his possession, he has the right to take the blood money, as he is now in the position of the first. If a crime is committed against the slave before the agent receives him, and the depositor takes the arsh, the agent may receive the slave but not the arsh. Similarly, if the depositor rents him out with the owner's permission, the agent does not take the rent. Similarly, the bride price of a slave woman if she is intercourse under dubious circumstances. If he authorizes him to receive a female slave or a sheep, and she gives birth, the agent may receive the offspring with the mother. If she gave birth before he authorized him to receive her, he does not have the right to receive the offspring. Similarly, the fruit of a garden is like the offspring. In al-Bada'i': As for the pillar of tawkil, it is offer and acceptance: the offer from the principal is that he says 'I appoint you agent for such-and-such' or 'do such-and-such' or 'I permit you to do such-and-such' and similar. Acceptance from the agent is that he says 'I accept' and what runs in its course. If it does not occur, it is not completed. For this reason, if a person authorizes someone to receive his debt, and he refuses to receive, then he goes and receives, the debtor is not discharged because he reneged by the refusal. Then the pillar may be absolute or conditional on a condition, like 'If Zayd comes, you are my agent for selling this.' End. Commentary on the statement: 'If he authorizes him to buy a specific thing, he should not buy it for himself' from al-Ramli: The distinction in the ruling between explicit acceptance and silence, so refer to it.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq compiles numerous specific rulings on the scope of the agent's authority depending on the wording used by the principal. The commentator draws from multiple sources (Khizanat al-Muftiyin, al-Bazzaziyya, Kafi al-Hakim, al-Bada'i', al-Ramli) to cover a wide range of scenarios. The underlying principle is that the agent's power is limited to what is explicitly or customarily included in the appointment, and any ambiguity is resolved by default interpretations. The key points: (1) 'You are my agent in everything' is interpreted as delegation of custody (hifz) only, by istihsan, because a general grant is ambiguous. (2) Adding 'your command is permissible' expands authority to sale, purchase, gift, and charity, but according to Imam Abu Hanifa, this does not include emancipation or gratuitous transfers; the fatwa is on this restriction. (3) Specific asset types: for income properties (mustaghallat), the agent can demand and collect rent; for debts, he can demand payment; for animals and slaves, he has custody and maintenance; for the wife, he can divorce but only in the same session (majlis), unlike if the principal said 'I give you possession' (milk) which is not session-restricted. (4) For managing a house, the agent cannot build or repair unless necessary for the purpose, and he is not automatically a litigant unless the need arises. (5) Agency for receiving debts: if a new debt arises after appointment, the agent is still authorized for it? The text says he is agent for its receipt if the wording is general. (6) For receiving a slave or animal, the agent can also receive offspring born after appointment, but not those born before. Similarly, fruit of a garden. (7) The passage ends with a quote from al-Bada'i' reiterating the pillar of tawkil (offer and acceptance) and noting that the pillar can be conditional. Finally, a note from al-Ramli distinguishes between explicit acceptance and silence when the agent is appointed to buy a specific item; the agent cannot buy it for himself. This rich section illustrates the Hanafi methodology of tasarruf (disposition) and the importance of wording in defining legal authority.

Key Terms
تفويض (tafwid): Delegation of authority; in this context, the principal entrusting the agent with certain powers
حفظ (hifz): Custody or preservation; the default scope when appointment is general
معاوضات (mu'awadat): Commutative transactions (sales, purchases) involving exchange of value
تقاضي (taqadi): Demanding payment or receipt of a debt

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, if a principal says 'You are my agent in everything,' what is the scope of the agent's authority by istihsan?
A) The agent can sell and buy all property.
B) The agent has authority only for custody (hifz).
C) The agent can divorce the principal's wife.
D) The agent can give charity from the principal's wealth.

Key Takeaway
The wording of the appointment determines the agent's authority: general phrases default to custody, while specific expansions or restrictions require explicit language.

The Scope of General Agency: 'أنت وكيلي في كل شيء' in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling on general agency authorization and its limits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the phrase 'أنت وكيلي في كل شيء' and distinguish between the scope of agency based on qiyas and istihsan.

Core Idea
A general agency phrase is limited to preservation by istihsan, overriding qiyas that would deem it invalid due to ignorance.

This lesson examines a classical Hanafi ruling on a commonly used agency statement: 'You are my agent in everything.' While a literal reading suggests blanket authority, Hanafi jurists applied istihsan to restrict it, illustrating the school's approach to ambiguous contracts. Understanding this distinction is crucial for determining the validity and limits of agency agreements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core phrase and its initial implication
The phrase 'أنت وكيلي في كل شيء' appears to grant unlimited agency. However, the Hanafi school interprets it restrictively, as the object is vague.
This vagueness (jihala) is key to the legal reasoning.
2
Understand the qiyas reasoning
Analogy (qiyas) would render the agency invalid (batil) because the scope is unknown, similar to any contract with unknown terms.
This is the default rule under general principles.
3
Apply istihsan to override qiyas
Istihsan (juristic preference) overrides the strict qiyas to validate the agency, but only for preservation (hifz) of property. This avoids hardship for the principal.
Istihsan is a distinctive Hanafi source of law.
4
Note the expansion when additional words are added
If the principal adds phrases like 'جائز أمرك' (your command is permissible), the agency expands to include sale, purchase, gift, and charity, but still within the principal's intent.
Additional specification clarifies the scope.
5
Identify the Imam's final restriction and the mufta bihi
Imam Abu Hanifa restricts the general agency to compensations (mu'awadat) and excludes emancipation and pure donations (tabarru'). This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
The text states 'وعليه الفتوى' — the fatwa is on this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إنفاذه ; كذا في خزانة المفتين. ولو قال أنت وكيلي في كل شيء كان تفويضاً للحفظ، والقياس أن لا يكون وكيلاً به للجهالة، والاستحسان انصرافها إلى الحفظ، ولو قال أجزت لك بيع هذا عبدي أنه يكون توكيلاً بالبيع ولو زاد على قوله أنت وكيلي في كل شيء جائز أمرك ملك الحفظ والبيع والشراء ويملك الهبة والصدقة حتى إذا أنفق على نفسه من ذلك المال جاز حتى يعلم خلافه من قصد الموكل . وعن الإمام تخصيصه بالمعاوضات ولا يلي العتق والتبرع وعليه الفتوى، وكذا إذا قال طلقت امرأتك ووقفت ووهبت أرضك في الأصح لا يجوز . وفي الروضة : فوضت أمري إليك قيل هذا باطل، وقيل هذا والأول سواء في أنه تفويض الحفظ.
Its execution? It is as in Khizanat al-Muftiyin. If he said 'You are my agent in everything', it is a delegation for preservation; analogy is that he is not agent due to ignorance; istihsan is that it turns to preservation. If he said 'I authorized you to sell this slave of mine', it becomes agency for sale, and if he added to his saying 'You are my agent in everything, your command is permissible', he owns preservation, sale, purchase, and he owns gift and charity, even if he spent from that wealth on himself it is permissible until he knows otherwise from the principal's intent. From Imam is its restriction to compensations, and he does not undertake emancipation and donation, and upon that is the fatwa. Similarly if he said 'You divorced your wife, and you endowed and gifted your land', in the most correct view it is not permissible. In al-Rawda: 'I delegated my affair to you' – some say this is invalid, some say this and the first are equal in that it is a delegation of preservation.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the legal effect of various phrases used to create agency. The author first addresses the phrase 'You are my agent in everything'. According to Hanafi law, such general wording is interpreted as a delegation for preservation (hifz) of property, not as authorization for all transactions. Analogy (qiyas) would suggest that no agency is created because the object is unknown (jihala), but the school prefers istihsan, which makes the agent authorized only to preserve the property. If the principal adds specific authorization like 'I authorized you to sell this slave', it constitutes agency for sale. However, the general authorization 'You are my agent in everything, your command is permissible' gives the agent authority over preservation, sale, purchase, gift, and charity, even spending on himself unless he knows the principal's intent to the contrary. Imam Abu Hanifa restricts this to compensations (mu'awadat) and excludes emancipation and pure donations (tabarru'). This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi). The text then notes that if the principal says 'You divorced your wife, endowed, and gifted your land', it does not create agency in the most correct view. Finally, the phrase 'I delegated my affair to you' is considered either invalid or equivalent to delegation for preservation only.

Key Terms
توكيل (tawkeel): A contract of agency where one person appoints another to act on his behalf.
تفويض (tafwidh): Delegation of authority, here specifically for preservation (hifz) of property.
استحسان (istihsan): A method of juristic preference that overrides qiyas in certain cases due to equity or necessity.
معاوضات (mu'awadat): Compensatory transactions, such as sale and purchase, where there is a exchange of value.
تبرع (tabarru'): Donation or gratuitous act, such as gift or charity, without compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what does the phrase 'أنت وكيلي في كل شيء' primarily establish?
A) Full agency for all transactions including sale and purchase
B) Delegation for preservation of property only
C) Agency for litigation and lawsuits
D) Authorization for emancipation and donations

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, general agency phrases are interpreted restrictively as delegation for preservation, and istihsan overrides qiyas to avoid nullifying the contract.

The Scope of Delegation with 'فوضت إليك'
Ruling on delegation scope with 'فوضت إليك'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the scope of authority for an agent when a principal uses the phrase 'فوضت إليك' with different objects: rental properties, debts, beasts/slaves, and the wife.

Core Idea
Scope of 'فوضت إليك' depends on the object; for the wife, divorce authority is session-limited.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the effects of a specific delegation phrase. Understanding these nuances prevents overstepping authority in agency contracts (wakalah). We'll explore how the same phrase yields different powers based on the object mentioned.

Guided Path
1
Identify the object of delegation
Determine what the principal is delegating: rental properties (mustaghallat), debts, beasts/slaves, or the wife. Each has a distinct default scope.
The phrase 'فوضت إليك أمر...' is consistent; the object changes the scope.
2
Determine the default scope for that category
For rental properties: demand and receive rent. For debts: demand payment. For beasts/slaves: preserve, herd, feed, and spend. For wife: divorce only.
The scope is limited to what is necessary for that object.
3
Note the session limitation for the wife
Authority to divorce the wife is restricted to the session (majlis) of delegation. This is a key exception.
The phrase 'ملكتك' would remove that limitation.
4
Distinguish from the stronger phrase 'ملكتك'
If the principal says 'ملكتك' (I made you owner), the agent's authority is not session-bound, contrasting with 'فوضت إليك'.
This distinction is specifically noted for the wife's case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا قال مالك المستغلات فوضت إليك أمر مستغلاتي وكان أجرها من إنسان ملك تقاضى الأجرة وقبضها، وكذا لو قال إليك أمر ديوني ملك التقاضي، ولو قال إليك فوضت أمر دوابي وأمر مماليكي ملك الحفظ والرعي والعلف والنفقة عليهم . فوضت إليك أمر امرأتي ملك طلاقها واقتصر على المجلس بخلاف قوله ملكتك حيث لا يقتصر على المجلس ؛ كذا في البزازية .
If the owner of rental properties says 'I delegated to you my rental properties', and their rent is with someone, he has the right to demand the rent and receive it. Similarly, if he says 'to you I delegated my debts', he has the right to demand payment. If he says 'I delegated to you my beasts and my slaves', he has the right of preservation, herding, feeding, and spending on them. If he says 'I delegated to you my wife', he has the right to divorce her, but it is limited to the session, unlike if he says 'I made you owner' (mallaktuka) where it is not limited to the session; as in al-Bazzaziyya.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage enumerates the effects of using the phrase 'فوضت إليك أمر' (I delegated to you the affair of) for different categories of property. For rental properties (mustaghallat), the agent gains authority to collect rent and its payment. For debts, the agent can demand payment from debtors. For beasts and slaves, the agent's authority includes preservation, herding, feeding, etc. For the wife, the agent gets authority to divorce her, but this authority is limited to the session of delegation, unlike if the principal says 'I made you owner' (mallaktuka) where the authority is not session-bound. This distinction is noted in al-Bazzaziyya.

Key Terms
مستغلات (mustaghallat): Rental properties that generate income.
تفويض (tafwidh): Delegation of authority, here used as a synonym for tawkeel (agency).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Unlimited authority over the wife including divorce and financial matters
B) Authority to divorce the wife, limited to the session of delegation
C) Authority to divorce the wife at any time, not limited to the session
D) Authority to manage the wife's property only

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'فوضت إليك' grants an agent specific authority tied to the object; for the wife, divorce authority is session-limited, unlike the phrase 'ملكتك'.

Limits of Agency in Property Management and Debt Collection
Rulings from Kafi al-Hakim on agency limits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific limitations of an agent's authority in managing property and collecting debts according to Hanafi rulings, and differentiate between rights acquired before and after the agency.

Core Idea
An agent's authority is strictly limited to what is explicitly granted; implicit powers are not assumed.

This passage from Kafi al-Hakim provides detailed clarifications on the scope of agency. While an agent may be authorized to manage property, collect produce, or demand debts, certain actions—such as structural repairs or litigation—require explicit permission. Understanding these boundaries prevents overstepping and ensures valid transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of agency discussed
The passage covers agency for property management (house) and for debt collection, as well as collection of deposits like slaves and animals. Note the scope of authorization in each case.
2
List permitted and prohibited actions for property management
From the text, extract what the agent can do (rent, collect produce, sell) and cannot do (build, repair, litigate). Recognize that litigation becomes permissible if a third party damages property in the agent's possession.
3
Analyze debt collection agency
If the agent is authorized to demand 'every debt he has', this includes debts arising after the agency. Understand the principle that general authorization covers future debts.
4
Examine rules for collecting deposits
For a slave or animal, determine when the agent can collect compensation (blood money, arsh, rent, mahr) and when it belongs to the principal. Note the distinction based on whether the item was already in the agent's possession.
5
Apply the rule on offspring and fruit
Offspring born after the agency are included in the collection; those born before are not. The same applies to fruit of a garden. This illustrates that the agent's authority covers what arises during the agency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي كافي الحاكم . لو وكله بالقيام على داره وإجارتها وقبض غلتها والبيع لم يكن له أن يبني ولا أن يرم منها شيئاً وليس وكيلاً في خصومتها، ولو هدم رجل منها شيئاً كان وكيلاً في الخصومة لأنه استهلك شيئاً في يديه، وكذا لو أجرها من رجل فجحد ذلك الرجل الإجارة كان خصماً فيها حتى يثبتها ، وكذا إذا سكنها وجحد وقال في باب الوكالة بالدين : لو وكله بتقاضي كل دين له ثم حدث له دين بعد ذلك الأجرا هـ. فهو وكيل في قبضه، ولو وكله بقبض غلة أرضه وثمرتها كان له أن يقبض ذلك كل سنة ا هـ . وقال في باب قبض الوديعة والعارية : ولو وكله بقبض عبد عند رجل فقتل العبد خطأ كان للمودع أن يأخذ القيمة من عاقلة القاتل وليس للوكيل أن يقبض القيمة لأنها كالثمن، ولو كان الوكيل قبض العبد فقتل عنده كان له أن يأخذ القيمة وهو الآن بمنزلة الأول، ولو جنى على العبد جناية قبل أن يقبضه الوكيل فأخذ المستودع أرشها فللوكيل أن يقبض العبد دون الأرش، وكذا لو كان المستودع آجره بإذن مولاه لم يأخذ الوكيل أجره، وكذا مهر الأمة إذا وطئت بشبهة . ولو وكله بقبض أمة أو شاة فولدت كان للوكيل أن يقبض الولد مع الأم ، ولو كانت ولدت قبل أن يوكله بقبضها لم يكن له أن يقبض الولد، وكذلك ثمرة البستان بمنزلة الولدا
And in Kafi al-Hakim: If he authorized him to manage his house, rent it, collect its produce, and sell, he does not have the right to build or repair anything from it, nor is he an agent for litigation regarding it. But if a person demolishes something from it, he becomes an agent for litigation because it was consumed in his hands. Similarly, if he rented it to a man and that man denied the rent, he is a litigant in it until he establishes it. Similarly if he occupied it and denied. And he said in the chapter of agency for debt: If he authorized him to demand every debt he has, then a debt arises after that, he is an agent for its collection. And if he authorized him to collect the produce of his land and its fruit, he may collect that every year. End. And he said in the chapter of collecting deposit and loan: If he authorized him to collect a slave from a man, and the slave was killed accidentally, the depositor may take the blood money from the 'aqila of the killer, and the agent cannot collect the blood money because it is like the price. But if the agent had received the slave and he was killed with him, he may take the blood money, and now it is like the first case. And if a tort was committed against the slave before the agent collected him, and the depositor took the arsh (compensation), the agent may collect the slave but not the arsh. Similarly, if the depositor rented him out with the permission of the owner, the agent does not take the rent. Similarly, the mahr of a slave woman if she is cohabited with due to shubha. If he authorized him to collect a female slave or a sheep and she gave birth, the agent may collect the offspring with the mother. But if she had given birth before he authorized him to collect her, he may not collect the offspring. Similarly, the fruit of a garden is like the offspring.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage from Kafi al-Hakim provides detailed rulings on agency for property management and debt collection. For managing a house, the agent is limited to renting, collecting produce, and selling; he cannot make structural changes (building or repairing) and is not automatically an agent for litigation. However, if a third party demolishes part of the house while in the agent's possession, the agent becomes a litigant to claim compensation. In debt collection, an agent appointed for all existing debts also covers debts arising after the appointment. For collecting produce and fruit, the authority is ongoing year after year. The section on collecting a deposit (like a slave) clarifies that if the slave is killed before collection, the depositor claims the blood money, not the agent. If collected and then killed, the agent can claim the blood money. Compensation for injury before collection goes to the depositor, not the agent. Similarly, rent and mahr belong to the principal. Offspring born after the agency are included, but not those born before. The same rule applies to fruit of a garden.

Key Terms
خصومة (khusumah): Litigation or legal dispute; here, whether the agent is authorized to represent the principal in court.
أرش (arsh): Compensation for injury or damage, typically a fraction of the value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text from Kafi al-Hakim, if an agent is authorized to manage a house (rent, collect produce, sell), what can he NOT do?
A) Collect rent from tenants
B) Sell the house
C) Build or repair anything from the house
D) Litigate against someone who demolishes part of the house

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi law of agency strictly limits the agent's authority to what is explicitly granted; any implied or expanded powers require separate authorization.

Rukn of Agency: Offer and Acceptance
Definition of the rukn of agency with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the rukn of agency in Hanafi law and distinguish between valid and invalid forms of offer and acceptance.

Core Idea
The rukn of agency is offer and acceptance; without both, the contract is void.

Agency (tawkeel) in Hanafi fiqh is a contract that depends on the mutual consent of the principal and agent. This consent is expressed through the pillars of offer (ijab) and acceptance (qabul). This lesson from al-Badai'i clarifies what constitutes a valid offer and acceptance, the effect of rejection, and how the pillar may be absolute, conditional, or time-bound.

Guided Path
1
Define the rukn of agency
State that the rukn is offer and acceptance. Understand that without either, the agency contract does not come into existence.
The Hanafi school considers offer and acceptance as the essential pillars.
2
Identify valid offer wordings
From the text, note the examples: 'I appoint you as agent for such and such', 'Do such and such', 'I permit you to do such and such'. Any clear wording indicating authorization suffices.
The offer must come from the principal.
3
Identify valid acceptance wordings
Acceptance is expressed by saying 'I accept' or any phrase that clearly indicates consent. The text says 'what runs in its course' – meaning equivalent expressions.
Acceptance must be explicit; conduct alone is insufficient.
4
Understand the effect of rejection
If the agent rejects the offer (e.g., refuses to collect a debt), the agency is nullified. Any subsequent action by that person is without authority, so the debtor is not discharged.
The rejection (radd) constitutes a termination of the offer.
5
Distinguish types of the pillar
The agency can be absolute (unrestricted), conditional (e.g., upon Zaid's arrival), or time-bound (e.g., starting tomorrow). Recognize that in a time-bound agency, the agent's authority begins only from the specified time.
The validity of conditional or time-bound agency depends on the clarity of the condition or time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي البدائع : وأما ركن التوكيل فهو الإيجاب والقبول؛ فالإيجاب من الموكل أن يقول وكلتك بكذا أو افعل كذا أو أذنت لك أن تفعل كذا ونحوه . والقبول من الوكيل أن يقول قبلت وما يجري مجراه فما لم يوجد لم يتم، ولهذا لو وكل إنساناً بقبض دينه فأبى أن يقبض ثم ذهب فقبض لم يبرأ الغريم لأنه ارتد بالرد. ثم الركن قد يكون مطلقاً وقد يكون معلقاً بشرط نحو إن قدم زيد فأنت وكيلي في بيع هذا العبد. وقد يكون مضافاً إلى وقت بأن يوكله في بيع هذا العبد غداً ويصير وكيلاً في الغد وما بعده لا قبله ا هـ .
And in al-Badai'i: As for the pillar (rukn) of agency, it is offer and acceptance. The offer from the principal is that he says 'I appoint you as agent for such and such' or 'do such and such' or 'I permit you to do such and such' and similar. The acceptance from the agent is that he says 'I accept' and what runs in its course. So if it does not exist, it is not complete. For this reason, if someone authorized a person to collect his debt and he refused to collect, then went and collected, the debtor is not discharged because he retracted by rejection. Then the pillar may be absolute, or conditional upon a condition like 'If Zaid comes, you are my agent for selling this slave.' And it may be added to a time, like he authorizes him to sell this slave tomorrow, and he becomes an agent tomorrow and after, not before. End.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage from al-Badai' describes the essential pillars (arkan) of the agency contract in Hanafi law. The rukn is the offer (ijab) from the principal and acceptance (qabul) from the agent. The offer can be in various wordings such as 'I appoint you as agent for...', 'Do...', or 'I permit you to...'. The acceptance must be explicit, like 'I accept' or equivalent. If the agent initially refuses and then collects, the debtor is not discharged because the rejection nullified the agency. The pillar can be absolute, conditional (e.g., upon the arrival of a person), or time-bound (e.g., starting tomorrow). In the latter case, the agent becomes agent only from the specified time onward.

Key Terms
ركن (rukn): An essential pillar of a contract; without it the contract is invalid.
إيجاب (ijab): The offer made by one party to initiate a contract.
قبول (qabul): The acceptance by the other party that completes the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The debtor is discharged because the agent collected

C) The debt is void
D) The agent becomes the owner of the debt

Key Takeaway
The rukn of agency in Hanafi law is offer and acceptance; rejection nullifies the offer and subsequent action by the agent is invalid.

Distinction Between Tawkeel and Irsal
Differentiating agency from mere message delivery in Hanafi law

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a wakil (agent) and a rasul (messenger), apply the Hanafi conditions for tawkeel, and identify which wordings create agency versus mere advice.

Core Idea
A wakil acts independently; a rasul merely conveys. Not every command creates agency—only those indicating deputyship.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq sharpens the distinction between two types of deputyship: tawkeel (agency) and irsal (sending a messenger). While both involve authorization, the wakil exercises independent authority in concluding contracts, whereas the rasul simply transmits the principal's instruction. The text also explores a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about whether certain imperative phrases constitute agency or message delivery, and provides practical examples of when a command does or does not create agency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two roles
First, understand the definitions: al-Qalanisi said the wakil directly executes the contract, while the rasul conveys the direct execution. The wakil acts in his own name for the principal; the rasul attributes the contract to the principal.
2
Analyze the wording that creates each
Second, examine the typical wordings: 'I sent you' or 'Be a messenger' indicates irsal. Phrases like 'Do such and such' or 'I command you to do such and such' indicate tawkeel according to the relied-upon view.
The dispute centers on 'I command you to collect it' (amartuka biqabdihi).
3
Distinguish commands that create agency from those that do not
Third, not every command is tawkeel. If the wording lacks an indication that the action is for the commander (e.g., 'buy this' without 'for me'), it is advice (mashura) and the purchase is for the commanded person, not the commander.
An exception is when a fee is stipulated, which signals deputyship (inabah).
4
Apply the principle to examples
Fourth, apply this to the examples from al-Walwalijiyya: 'Buy for me with it' creates agency; 'Buy with it' without 'for me' does not. 'Buy a slave-girl with this thousand' pointing to the commander's wealth also does not create agency unless 'for me' is added or a fee is promised.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قلت : فما الفرق بين التوكيل والإرسال فإن الإذن والأمر توكيل كما علمت؟ قلت : الرسول أن يقول له أرسلتك أو كن رسولاً عني في كذا وقد جعل منها الزيلعي في باب خيار الرؤية أمرتك بقبضه . وصرح في النهاية فيه معزياً إلى الفوائد الظهيرية أنه من التوكيل وهو الموافق لما في البدائع إذ لا فرق بين افعل كذا وأمرتك بكذا. واعلم أنه ليس كل أمر يفيد التوكيل كان فيما أمر به ففي الولوالجية؛ دفع له ألفاً وقال اشتر لي بها أو بع أو قال اشتر بها أو بع ولم يقل لي كا توكيلاً، وكذا اشتر بهذا الألف جارية، وأشار إلى مال نفسه، ولو قال اشتر جارية بألف درهم كانت مشورة وما اشتراه المأمور فهو له دون الآمر، وكذا لو قال اشتر هذه بألف إلا إذا زاد على أن أعطيك لأجل شرائك درهماً لأن اشتراط الأجر له يدل على الإنابة ا هـ . وفي تهذيب القلانسي : الوكيل من يباشر العقد والرسول من يبلغ المباشرة والسلعة أمانة في أيديهما ا هـ .
If you ask: What is the difference between tawkeel (agency) and irsal (sending)? For permission and command are tawkeel as you have learned. I answer: The messenger (rasul) is one to whom he says 'I sent you' or 'Be a messenger from me for such and such'. Al-Zayla'i included in the chapter of khiyar al-ru'ya 'I commanded you to collect it' as from it. And he explicitly stated in al-Nihaya, attributing to al-Fawa'id al-Zahiriyya, that it is from tawkeel, which matches what is in al-Badai', since there is no difference between 'do such and such' and 'I command you to do such and such'. Know that not every command constitutes tawkeel for what he is commanded to do. In al-Walwalijiyya: He gave him a thousand and said 'Buy for me with it' or 'Sell' or he said 'Buy with it' or 'Sell' and did not say 'for me', it is not tawkeel. Similarly, 'Buy a slave-girl with this thousand', pointing to his own wealth, and if he said 'Buy a slave-girl for a thousand dirhams', it is advice, and what the commanded person buys is for himself, not the commander. Similarly, if he said 'Buy this for a thousand' unless he added 'I will give you a dirham for your purchase', because stipulating a fee indicates deputyship. In Tahdhib al-Qalanisi: The wakil (agent) is the one who directly executes the contract; the rasul (messenger) is the one who conveys the direct execution, and the commodity is a trust in both their hands.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage clarifies the distinction between agency (tawkeel) and mere message delivery (irsal) in Hanafi law. The fundamental difference is that an agent (wakil) acts on his own authority in concluding a contract, while a messenger (rasul) merely conveys the principal's instruction. However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute as to whether phrases like 'I command you to collect' (amartuka biqabdihi) constitute agency or message delivery. Al-Zayla'i considered it as part of irsal, but the author of al-Nihaya, citing al-Fawa'id al-Zahiriyya, holds that it is tawkeel, consistent with al-Badai' which sees no difference between 'do' and 'I command you'. Not every command creates agency; if the wording does not indicate that the action is on behalf of the commander (e.g., 'buy this' without 'for me'), it is merely advice (mashura) or a non-binding suggestion unless a fee is offered, which indicates deputyship. The practical consequence is that an agent acts in his own name for the principal, while a messenger simply transmits the principal's direct action.

Key Terms
رسول (rasul): A messenger who merely conveys the principal's direct instruction without independent authority.
وكيل (wakil): An agent who concludes contracts on behalf of the principal with his own authority.
إنابة (inabah): Deputyship or commission; stipulating a fee indicates that the person is acting as a deputy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Irsal, because it is a command without deputyship.
B) Tawkeel, because there is no difference between 'افعل كذا' and 'أمرتك بكذا'.
C) Advice (mashura), because it lacks a fee.
D) Invalid, because it is ambiguous.

Key Takeaway
A wakil acts independently; a rasul merely conveys; not every command creates agency—only those indicating deputyship (e.g., 'for me' or a fee).
