Resolving the Objection: Father's Delegation of Purchase for Minor
Objection and response regarding father's delegation of purchase for minor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits a father to delegate purchase for his minor child only as part of a sale authorization, and apply this distinction to other guardianship scenarios.

Core Idea
A father cannot delegate pure purchase of his child's property, but incidental purchase within sale authorization is valid.

This passage addresses a subtle objection to the general rule that a principal can delegate an act he can perform himself. The father can buy for his child directly, so why can't he authorize someone else to buy? The commentator resolves this by distinguishing between a pure purchase agency and a purchase that is incidental to a sale authorization. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the rules of agency in guardianship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
What is the objection raised against the rule? The objection is that the father can buy for his child himself, so he should be able to delegate that purchase.
The objection is based on the general principle of agency.
2
State the apparent contradiction
There appears to be a contradiction between al-Siraj (which says the father cannot own his child's property via pure purchase agency) and al-Tabyin (which seems to allow it in a certain context).
The two texts need reconciliation.
3
Follow the commentator's resolution
How does the commentator reconcile the two? By showing that al-Tabyin refers to purchase within a sale authorization, not pure purchase agency.
The key is the intention (qasdan) in al-Siraj: 'intentionally' acquiring via purchase delegation.
4
Apply the distinction
Use the example from Hashiyat Abi al-Su'ud: father says 'I authorize you to sell my son's slave to me'. This is valid because the purchase is incidental to the sale authorization.
The father's purchase is part of the sale transaction.
5
Derive the principle
The father's special status as guardian does not give him broader agency rights; it only allows direct transactions. Delegation requires the same conditions as any principal.
The distinction preserves the validity of the original rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لكن يرد عليه الأب والجد الخ) وفي التبيين قبيل الغصب أنه لا فلا شيخنا : ثم ظهر لي تسليم الورود وأنه لا مخالفة بين ما في السراج والتبيين، وذلك أن ما في السراج أنه لا يملك تملك مال ولده بالتوكيل بشرائه أي قصداً وما في التبيين إنما ملك تملكه لكونه في ضمن التوكيل ببيعه فملك الشراء من وكله بالبيع .اهـ. فإن قال الأب لشخص وكلتك ببيع عبد ابني مني ؛ ؛ كذا في حاشية أبي السعود
His saying: (but it is objected by the case of the father and grandfather etc.) And in al-Tabyin before the chapter of al-Ghasb that... no so our teacher: then it became clear to me to accept the objection and that there is no contradiction between what is in al-Siraj and al-Tabyin. That is, what is in al-Siraj that he does not own acquiring the property of his child through authorization for its purchase, i.e., intentionally, and what is in al-Tabyin is that he only owned acquiring it because it is within the authorization for its sale, so he owned the purchase from the one he authorized to sell. End. So if the father says to a person: I authorize you to sell my son's slave from me...; thus in Hashiyat Abi al-Su'ud.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection regarding the ضابط of agency: the father and grandfather can buy property for their minor child directly, but they cannot authorize another person to do so on their behalf. This seems to contradict the ضابط that 'he can contract by himself' implies he can authorize it. The commentator resolves this by citing al-Tabyin and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: there is no contradiction. The father can authorize someone to buy for his child only indirectly when that authorization is incidental to a sale authorization (e.g., he authorizes someone to sell and that person also buys). The direct authorization for purchase alone is not covered because the father does not intend to acquire the child's property via agency; he can only do it himself. This subtle distinction preserves the validity of the ضابط. The commentator later adds a concrete example: if the father says to someone, 'I authorize you to sell my son's slave to me,' this is a valid sale authorization that includes the father's purchase, but it is not a pure purchase authorization. So the objection is resolved.

Key Terms
الأب والجد (al-ab wa al-jadd): The father and paternal grandfather: they have guardianship (wilayah) over the minor's property and can transact directly but not delegate pure purchase.
تملك (tamalluk): Acquiring ownership; here it refers to the father acquiring the child's property for himself via agency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, how is the apparent contradiction between al-Siraj and al-Tabyin resolved?
A) Al-Siraj is wrong and al-Tabyin is correct.
B) Al-Siraj refers to pure purchase agency, while al-Tabyin refers to purchase incidental to a sale authorization.
C) The father cannot buy at all from his child.
D) The father can always delegate purchase to anyone.

Key Takeaway
The father's ability to buy directly for his child does not automatically allow him to delegate pure purchase; only incidental purchase within a sale authorization is valid.

Tawkeel bi al-Istiqrad: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on agency for borrowing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on tawkeel bi al-istiqrad, compare the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and state the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
Appointing an agent to borrow is invalid in Zahir al-Riwayah, but Abu Yusuf and later authorities permit it—the dispute turns on the subject of the agency.

Agency (wakalah) is generally permitted for any contract one can perform oneself. But can you appoint someone to borrow money on your behalf? The Hanafi school has a classic internal difference: Imam Abu Hanifa ruled it invalid, while Imam Abu Yusuf permitted it. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning, the practical consequences, and how later scholars resolved the issue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Recognise that the issue is tawkeel bi al-istiqrad: appointing an agent to borrow money on one's behalf.
This is a specific sub-topic in the chapter of wakalah.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his dalil
Abu Hanifa holds that such agency is invalid because the subject of the agency (mahall al-'aqd) is the borrowed money, which is not owned by the principal at the time of contract. Ordering disposal of another's property is invalid.
Also, if the agent attributes the borrowing to himself, the debt becomes his own.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position and his dalil
Abu Yusuf holds it valid. He argues that the subject of the agency is the principal's expression (ibarah al-muwakkil), making the agent a mere intermediary (safir), analogous to marriage agency.
The borrowed funds can be attributed to the principal if the agent expressly does so.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, if the agent borrows, it is for himself unless he expressly says 'I borrow for my principal'. Under Abu Yusuf, the agency is valid and the principal is bound if the agent acts within authority.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi authorities (al-Kasani, al-Zayla'i, and Ibn Nujaym) adopt the permissibility view, making it the relied-upon position for fatwa.
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq wrote a treatise supporting this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يمكن طرده عدم توكيل الذمي مسلماً ببيع خمره وهو يملكه لأنه يملك التوصل به بتوكيل الذمي به فصدق الضابط لأنه لم يقل كل عقد يملكه يملك توكيل كل أحد به بل التوصل به في الجملة، وإنما يرد عليه توكيل الوكيل بلا إذن وتعميم فإنه يملك العقد الذي وكل به ولا يملك التوكيل. وأجابوا بأن المراد لنفسه لكن يرد عليه الأب والجد يملكان شراء مال ولده الصغير ولا يملكان التوكيل به كما في السراج الوهاج والاستقراض فإنه يباشره بنفسه لنفسه ولا يملك التوكيل به فيقع للوكيل؛ كذا ذكر الشارح. ولم يجب عنه والجواب منع عدم صحته به لما في الخانية : إن وكل بالاستقراض فإن أضاف الوكيل الاستقراض إلى الموكل كان للموكل وإلا كان بموجود في التوكيل بالاستقراض لأن الدراهم التي يستقرضها الوكيل ملك المقرض والأمر بالتصرف في ملك الغير باطل، وهذا من باب التخلف المانع. وقيد عدم المانع في الأحكام الكلية غير لازم وعن أبي يوسف أن التوكيل بالاستقراض جائز فعلى هذا لا نقض به على مذهبه فليتأمل .اهـ. وقال في أواخر الفصل التاسع كتاب نور العين جف بعث رجلاً ليستقرضه فأقرضه فضاع في يده فلو قال أقرض للمرسل ضمن مرسله ولو قال أقرضني للمرسل ضمن رسوله والحاصل أن التوكيل بالإقراض جائز لا بالاستقراض، والرسالة بالاستقراض تجوز ولو أخرج وكيل الاستقراض كلامه مخرج الرسالة يقع القرض للأمر، ولو مخرج الوكالة بأن أضافه إلى نفسه يقع للوكيل وله منعه من أمره. يقول الحقير: إنما لم يجوزوا التوكيل بالاستقراض ظناً أنه لا محل فيه لعقد الوكالة، وقد أطال شراح الهداية الكلام في هذا المقام، وفي زمان تدريسي كنت كتبت في هذا المبحث رسالة طويلة الذيول لطيفة بحيث قبلها كثير من الفحول وحاصلها أن محل العقد فيه عبارة الموكل كما في التوكيل بالنكاح ونحوه مما يكون فيه الوكيل سفيراً محضاً فلا بأس أصلاً في أن تسمى الرسالة بالاستقراض وكالة كما تسمى الرسالة بالنكاح ونحوه وكالة ويؤيد ما ذكرناه ما قال الإمام الكاشاني في البدائع : ويجوز التوكيل في القرض والاستقراض. وما قال الإمام الزيلعي أيضاً في شرح الكنز : وعن أبي يوسف أن التوكيل بالاستقراض جائز لا يقال لو كان وكالة لما دفع للموكل فيما إذا أضافه إلى نفسه لأنا نقول : حال الوكالة بالشراء أيضاً كذلك لأن الوكيل بشراء شيء لا بعينه إذا اشتراه يكون هو له إلا أن ينوي الشراء لموكله إذ العقد إلى دراهم موكله كما ذكر في الهداية وغيرها والله تعالى أعلم اهـ
وزعم الإعطاء وأقر الرسول وأنكر المستقرض دفع المقرض لا يلزم المستقرض شيء ا هـ . ثم قال بعده : صح التوكيل بالإقراض لا بالاستقراض. وفي القنية : التوكيل بالاستقراض لا يصح؛ والتوكيل بقبض القرض يصح بأن يقول لرجل أقرضني ثم يوكل رجلاً بقبضه يصح ولو قال المصنف بكل ما يباشره لكان أولى ليشمل العقد وغيره فكان يستغني عن أفراد بعض الأشياء. اهـ.
It is possible to refute [the objection of] the invalidity of a dhimmi appointing a Muslim to sell his wine while he owns it, because he can achieve it by appointing a dhimmi to do it, so the principle holds because it did not say 'every contract that he can perform, he can appoint anyone to do it', but rather 'he can achieve it in general'. However, it is objected that the agent cannot appoint another without permission and general authorization, for he can perform the contract he was appointed to but cannot appoint another. They answered that the intended meaning is 'for himself', but the objection remains regarding the father and grandfather: they can purchase the property of their minor child but cannot appoint an agent for it, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, and regarding borrowing: one performs it himself for himself and cannot appoint an agent for it, so it falls to the agent; thus mentioned the commentator. And he did not answer it. The answer is to deny its invalidity because in al-Khaniyya: If he appoints an agent for borrowing, then if the agent attributes the borrowing to the principal, it is for the principal; otherwise it is for the agent. End. And in al-Bazzaziyya: He borrowed a thousand from him and ordered him to give it to his messenger so-and-so... [some unclear text]... He said: it invalidates the refutation. His statement: 'But the father and grandfather are objected...' and in al-Tabyin before ghasb that... so our teacher: Then it became apparent to me to accept the objection, and there is no conflict between what is in al-Siraj and al-Tabyin, because what is in al-Siraj is that he cannot own the property of his child by appointing an agent to purchase it, i.e., intentionally, and what is in al-Tabyin is that he only owns it because it is within the appointment to sell it, so he purchases from the one who appointed him to sell. End. If the father says to a person: I appoint you to sell the slave of my son to me... likewise in the gloss of Abu al-Su'ud. His statement: 'And the answer is to deny its invalidity by it...' He said in al-Hawashi al-Ya'qubiyya: And borrowing is not objected because the subject of the contract is among its conditions, and it is not present in appointment for borrowing because the dirhams that the agent borrows are owned by the lender, and ordering disposal in another's property is invalid, and this is from the category of a preventing deficiency. And the condition of absence of preventer in general rulings is not necessary. And from Abu Yusuf that appointment for borrowing is permissible, so on this there is no criticism of his school, so reflect. End. And he said at the end of the ninth chapter of the book Nur al-Ayn: He sent a man to borrow for him, so he lent him and it was lost in his hand; if he said 'lend to the sender', the sender is liable; if he said 'lend to me the sender', his messenger is liable. The conclusion is that appointment for lending is permissible, not for borrowing, and sending for borrowing is permissible. If the agent for borrowing phrases his words as a message, the loan falls to the commander; if as agency by attributing to himself, it falls to the agent, and he can prevent him from his command. The humble one says: They did not permit appointment for borrowing only due to the assumption that there is no subject for the agency contract. The commentators of al-Hidayah have long discussed this topic, and during my teaching period I wrote a lengthy treatise on this investigation, refined, accepted by many scholars. Its conclusion is that the subject of the contract therein is the expression of the principal, as in appointment for marriage and similar matters where the agent is a mere intermediary, so there is no problem in calling the message for borrowing an agency, just as the message for marriage and similar matters is called an agency. And it supports what we mentioned what Imam al-Kasani said in al-Bada'i': And appointment for lending and borrowing is permissible. And what Imam al-Zayla'i also said in Sharh al-Kanz: And from Abu Yusuf that appointment for borrowing is permissible. It cannot be said that if it were agency, it would not be given to the principal when he attributes it to himself, for we say: the case of agency for purchase is also similar, because the agent for purchasing something unspecified, if he buys it, it is for him unless he intends to buy for his principal, since the contract is based on the dirhams of his principal, as mentioned in al-Hidayah and others. And Allah knows best. End.
He claimed the giving, and the messenger affirmed, and the borrower denied the payment; the lender is not obligated anything. End. Then he said after it: Appointment for lending is valid, not for borrowing. And in al-Quniyah: Appointment for borrowing is not valid; appointment for receiving a loan is valid, such that he says to a man: lend to me, then he appoints a man to receive it - it is valid. If the author had said 'by everything he performs himself', it would be better to include the contract and others, and he would be independent from specifying some things. End.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, commenting on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It addresses the principle of tawkeel (appointment of an agent): a person can appoint an agent for any action they themselves can perform. However, objections arise in specific cases. The first is a dhimmi appointing a Muslim to sell wine: the dhimmi owns the wine, but the Muslim cannot own it for sale? The response is that the principle allows achieving the act in general, not every detail. A stronger objection is that an agent cannot sub-delegate without permission, and the father/grandfather cannot appoint an agent to buy property for their minor child even though they can do it themselves. The commentator clarifies that the father can buy the child's property if it comes within a sale appointment (e.g., the child's agent appointed to sell, the father buys). For borrowing (istiqrad), the early view is that one cannot appoint an agent to borrow because the agent would be dealing with the lender's money, not the principal's. The agent's action would be on his own behalf unless he phrases it as a message. Abu Yusuf allows appointment for borrowing, and later scholars like al-Kasani and al-Zayla'i support this, reasoning that the subject of the agency is the principal's expression, making the agent a mere intermediary, similar to marriage agency. The passage also distinguishes between appointment for lending (iqrad) which is valid, and for borrowing which is disputed. The author (Ibn Nujaym) mentions his own treatise supporting permissibility. Practical takeaway: Appointing someone to borrow is problematic as true agency but can work as a message; if the agent says 'I borrow for my principal' it's valid according to Abu Yusuf and later fatwa.

Key Terms
الوكالة (al-wikalah): Appointment of another to perform a legally valid act on one's behalf.
الاستقراض (al-istiqrad): The act of borrowing money; in agency context, appointing someone to take a loan on one's behalf.
الإقراض (al-iqrad): Lending; appointing someone to lend money on one's behalf.
محل العقد (mahall al-'aqd): The subject matter of the contract; in agency, what the agent is authorized to transact.
الرسالة (al-risalah): Being a mere messenger or intermediary, as opposed to a true agent with delegated authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school, which of the following is correct regarding tawkeel bi al-istiqrad?
A) It is invalid under any circumstances.
B) It is valid, following Abu Yusuf and later authorities.
C) It is valid only if the agent is also the lender.
D) It is invalid unless the money is physically present.

Key Takeaway
Tawkeel bi al-istiqrad is permissible in the relied-upon Hanafi view, provided the agent properly attributes the borrowing to the principal.

Ruling on Lender's Claim and Messenger's Acknowledgment
Ruling on dispute between lender, messenger, borrower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a messenger acknowledges receipt but the borrower denies it, and explain why the messenger's statement cannot impose liability on the borrower.

Core Idea
The messenger's acknowledgment clears himself but cannot bind the borrower who denies receipt.

When a lender claims he entrusted money to a messenger, and the messenger confirms receiving it, but the borrower insists he never received it, a conflict arises. Whose word is accepted? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position: the borrower's denial prevails, and the messenger's statement only protects his own trust, not the borrower's liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their claims
There are three parties: the lender (who claims he gave the money), the messenger (who acknowledges receipt from the lender), and the borrower (who denies receiving it). The core question is whether the lender's claim and messenger's acknowledgment can obligate the borrower to pay.
The messenger is an agent for delivery, not a party to the loan.
2
Determine the legal status of the messenger
The messenger is considered a trustee (ameen) in Hanafi law. As a trustee, his word is accepted regarding his own actions and liabilities, but not to establish claims against others.
This principle applies to all trustees (e.g., custodians, partners) unless there is evidence to the contrary.
3
Apply the rule to the borrower
The borrower denies receiving the money. His denial is a valid defense because the burden of proof is on the lender or his agent. The messenger's acknowledgment cannot override the borrower's denial because the messenger is not a witness against the borrower; he is a trustee for the lender.
If the borrower had acknowledged receipt, he would be liable.
4
Conclude the ruling
Therefore, the borrower is not obligated to pay anything. The messenger is also not liable because his word is accepted to prove his own innocence (i.e., that he delivered the money) but that does not make the borrower liable. The lender must pursue the borrower with evidence if he wishes to claim receipt.
Had the messenger failed to deliver, his trust would be questioned, but here he claims delivery.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزعم الإعطاء وأقر الرسول وأنكر المستقرض دفع المقرض لا يلزم المستقرض شيء ا هـ . قوله : ( وزعم) أي المقرض وقوله وأقر الرسول أي بالقبض رملي قوله : (لا يلزم المستقرض شيء) قال الرملي : وهل يلزم الرسول الجواب؟ لا لأنه أمين يقبل قوله في حق براءة نفسه لا في لزوم الدين ذمة المستقرض كرسول المديون بالدين إلى الدائن إذا أنكر وصوله إليه وادعى الرسول إيصاله إليه يقبل قوله في حق نفسه لا في حق براءة الدائن تأمل.
And the lender claims the giving, and the messenger acknowledges, and the borrower denies, the payment of the lender does not obligate the borrower anything. His saying: (And the claim) meaning the lender, and his saying: and the messenger acknowledged, meaning the receipt by Ramli. His saying: (the borrower is not obligated anything) said al-Ramli: Is the messenger obligated to answer? No, because he is a trustee; his statement is accepted regarding his own innocence, not regarding the obligation of debt in the borrower's liability, like the messenger of the debtor with the debt to the creditor when he denies its arrival and the messenger claims he delivered it; his statement is accepted regarding himself, not regarding the creditor's innocence, ponder.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement. The matn states that if the lender claims he gave the money, the messenger (agent) acknowledges receipt, but the borrower denies receiving it from the lender, then the borrower is not liable to pay anything. The commentary clarifies that the word 'claim' refers to the lender. The messenger's acknowledgment is about receipt, as stated by Ramli. The messenger is not required to answer (i.e., be liable) because he is an ameen (trustee). His word is accepted to prove his own innocence, but not to impose a debt on the borrower. This is analogous to a messenger of a debtor sent to pay a creditor: if the creditor denies receiving payment and the messenger claims delivery, the messenger's word is accepted to clear himself, not to free the debtor from liability.

Key Terms
زعم (za'ama): A claim or assertion, here used for the lender's claim of giving the money.
أمين (ameen): A trustee; here the messenger is considered an ameen, so his statement is accepted regarding his own liability but not to bind others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a lender claims he gave money to a messenger to pay a borrower, the messenger acknowledges receipt, but the borrower denies receiving it, what is the ruling?
A) The borrower must pay because the messenger acknowledged.
B) The borrower is not liable, and the messenger is not liable either.
C) The borrower is not liable, but the messenger must pay.
D) The lender must prove both giving and receipt.

Key Takeaway
The messenger's acknowledgment is accepted to protect his own trust, but it cannot impose liability on the borrower who denies receipt.

Agency for Lending vs. Borrowing
Ruling on validity of agency for lending and borrowing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on agency for lending and borrowing, distinguish the validity of each, and identify the exception for receiving a loan.

Core Idea
Agency for lending is valid; agency for borrowing is not, because borrowing creates personal liability.

This lesson clarifies a key distinction in the Hanafi law of agency: while one may authorize another to lend one's own money, one cannot authorize another to borrow on one's behalf. The reason lies in the nature of the contract—lending is a pure disposition of property, whereas borrowing creates a debt obligating the borrower personally. However, an important nuance is that after arranging a loan oneself, one can appoint an agent to receive the money.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts
Distinguish between 'iqrad' (lending) and 'istiqrad' (borrowing). Lending means giving money as a loan; borrowing means taking a loan.
2
State the ruling for each
Agency for lending is valid (sahih) because it involves disposal of property. Agency for borrowing is invalid (fasid) because borrowing creates a personal debt obligation.
3
Understand the exception
Agency to receive a loan is valid if the principal has already arranged the loan, e.g., saying 'Lend to me' and then appointing an agent to receive the money.
This is not the same as agency to borrow; the debt obligation is already incurred by the principal.
4
Consider the commentator's suggestion
Al-Qunyah notes that the author could have used a general phrase like 'agency for everything the principal does himself' to cover both lending and receiving, avoiding the need to specify individual cases.
This highlights the principle that agency is valid for acts the principal can perform personally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قال بعده : صح التوكيل بالإقراض لا بالاستقراض. وفي القنية : التوكيل بالاستقراض لا يصح؛ والتوكيل بقبض القرض يصح بأن يقول لرجل أقرضني ثم يوكل رجلاً بقبضه يصح ولو قال المصنف بكل ما يباشره لكان أولى ليشمل العقد وغيره فكان يستغني عن أفراد بعض الأشياء. اهـ.
Then he said after that: Agency for lending is valid, not for borrowing. And in al-Qunyah: Agency for borrowing is not valid; and agency for receiving the loan is valid by him saying to a man 'Lend to me' then he appoints an agent to receive it, it is valid. And if the author had said 'with everything he does himself' it would have been better to include the contract and other things, and he would have been independent from specifying some things.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage states that agency for lending (i.e., authorizing someone to lend one's money to another) is valid, but agency for borrowing (i.e., authorizing someone to borrow on one's behalf) is not valid. The reason is that borrowing creates a debt and an obligation, which is not a pure act of disposition; it requires the borrower's personal consent. However, agency to receive a loan that one has already arranged is valid. For example, one says to a person 'Lend to me' and then appoints an agent to receive the money; this is valid. The commentator notes that if the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq had used a general phrase like 'agency for everything the principal does himself,' it would have covered both lending and receiving, and he would not need to specify individual cases.

Key Terms
إقراض (iqrad): Lending: the act of giving money as a loan.
استقراض (istiqrad): Borrowing: the act of taking a loan.
قبض القرض (qabd al-qard): Receiving the loan: taking possession of the loaned money.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Is it valid for someone to appoint an agent to borrow money on their behalf?
A) Yes, because borrowing is a financial transaction.
B) No, because agency for borrowing is invalid.
C) Yes, but only if the agent is also the lender.
D) No, but agency to receive a loan is valid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, agency for lending is valid, but agency for borrowing is invalid because borrowing creates a personal liability that cannot be delegated; however, agency to receive a loan already arranged by the principal is valid.

Agency in Litigation and the Consent of the Opponent
Inter-madhhab dispute on requiring opponent's consent for agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on requiring the opponent's consent for agency in litigation, explain the disagreement with the Sahibayn, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah) of the dispute.

Core Idea
The opponent's consent is required for binding agency in litigation, except for those unable to attend court.

This passage addresses a foundational question in Islamic procedural law: can a litigant appoint an agent without the consent of his opponent? The Hanafi school has an important internal dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding the reasoning behind each position reveals how different analogies (qiyas) lead to different rulings and highlights the delicate balance between a party's right to respond and the need for flexibility. This lesson unpacks the dispute and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Identify that according to Abu Hanifa, agency in litigation (al-wakalah bi al-khusumah) is valid but binding only with the opponent's consent. Note the exceptions: sick, traveler, intending to travel, and woman in seclusion.
The passage explicitly attributes this to Abu Hanifa.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) hold that the agency is valid and binding without the opponent's consent. The dispute is about luzum (bindingness), not jawaz (permissibility).
The text says: 'There is no dispute about permissibility, only about bindingness.'
3
Analyze the opponent's proof
The Sahibayn argue that agency is a disposition in one's own right, so it does not depend on another's consent, analogous to agency for collecting debts.
This is a qiyas based on 'tasarruf fi khalis haqqihi'.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa argues that the opponent has a right to personally respond, as 'people vary in litigation ability.' Forcing an agent would cause harm, analogous to a jointly owned slave's kitabah where the other co-owner has an option. The response is a duty owed to the opponent, so his consent is needed.
The analogy to al-'abd al-mushtarak is key.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If a defendant appoints an agent without consent, Abu Hanifa says the plaintiff can refuse and demand the defendant appear; the Sahibayn say the plaintiff must accept the agent.
This practical difference affects court procedure directly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وبالخصومة في الحقوق برضا الخصم إلا أن يكون الموكل مريضاً أو غائباً مدة السفر أو مريداً للسفر أو مخدرة) أي وصح التوكيل بالخصومة بشرط رضا الخصم وهذا عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : يجوز بغير رضاه ولا خلاف في الجواز إنما الخلاف في اللزوم؛ لهما أن التوكيل تصرف في خالص حقه فلا يتوقف على رضا غيره كالتوكيل بتقاضي الديون، وله أن الجواب مستحق على الخصم ولهذا يستحضره والناس متفاوتون في الخصومة، فلو قلنا بلزومه يتضرر به فيتوقف على رضاه كالعبد المشترك إذا كاتبه أحدهما يتخير الآخر بخلاف المريض والمسافر لأن الجواب غير مستحق عليهما هنالك ومريده كهو لتحقيق الضرورة، والمخدرة لو حضرت لا يمكنها أن تنطق بحقها لحيائها فيلزم توكيلها وهذا شيء استحسنه المتأخرون؛ كذا في الهداية. وظاهره أن المخدرة لا نص عليها في المذهب ولهذا قال في فتح القدير: أما على ظاهر إطلاق الأصل وغيره عن أبي حنيفة فلا فرق بين البكر والثيب والمخدرة والمبرزة والفتوى على ما اختاروه من ذلك ا.هـ. والخصومة الجدل، خاصمه مخاصمة وخصومة فخصمه يخصمه غلبه وهو شاذ لأن فاعلته ففعلته يرد يفعل منه إلى الضم إن لم تكن عينه حرف حلق فإنه بالفتح كفاخره فقخره يفخره، أما المعتل كوجدت وبعت فيرد إلى الكسر إلا ذوات الواو فإنها ترد إلى الضم كراضيته فرضوته أرضوه وخاوفني فخفته أخوفه، وليس في كل شيء يقال نازعته لأنهم استغنوا عنه بغلبته . واختصموا تخاصموا والخصم المخاصم والجمع الخصوم، وقد يكون للجمع والاثنين والمؤنث والخصم المخاصم والجمع خصماء؛ في القاموس . هذا معناها لغة . وأما شرعاً فهو الجواب بنعم أو لا كما سيأتي . وفسرها في الجوهرة بالدعوى الصحيحة أو بالجواب الصريح ولو وكله في الخصومة له لا عليه فله كذا قوله: (ولا خلاف في الجواز إنما الخلاف في اللزوم قال في الجوهرة: يعني هل ترد الوكالة إثبات ما للموكل، فلو أراد المدعى عليه الدفع لم تسمع ؛ كذا في منية المفتي. والحاصل أنها تتخصص بتخصيص الموكل وتعمم بتعميمه، والألف واللام في الحقوق للجنس فشمل بعضاً معيناً وجميعها. وفي القنية : لو رضي ثم مضى يوم فقال لا أرضى له ذلك اهـ. وذكره في شرح المجمع معزياً إليها والتقييد باليوم اتفاقي وإنما المقصود أن له الرجوع عن الرضا ما لم يسمع القاضي الدعوى لما في القنية أيضاً : لو ادعى وكيل المدعي عند القاضي ثم أتى بشهود ليقيمها ولم يرض الخصم أي المدعي عليه بالوكيل ويريد أن يخاصم مع الخصم ليس له ذلك بعد سماع الدعوى على أصل أبي حنيفة. وفي البزازية ولو وكله بكل حق هو له وبخصومته. في كل حق له ولم يعين المخاصم به والمخاصم فيه جاز ا هـ . وإذا وكله بقبض كل حق يحدث له والخصومة فيه جائز أمره فإنه يدخل فيه الدين والوديعة والعارية وكل حق ملكه الموكل، أما النفقة فمن الحقوق التي لا يملكها كذا في الخزانة. وفي الولوالجية : وكله بالخصومة ولم يبين أي الخصومة لم تجز الوكالة لأنها تقع في الأجناس المختلفة . وأطلق في الخصم فشمل الطالب والمطلوب كما شملهما الموكل، والشريف والوضيع كما في البزازية. وأطلق المريض وهو مقيد بما إذا كان لا يقدر على المشي على قدميه إلى مجلس القاضي مدعياً كان أو مدعى عليه، وإن قدر على الحضور على ظهر الدابة أو ظهر إنسان فإن زاد مرضه بذلك لزم توكيله فإن لم يزد قيل على الخلاف والصحيح لزومه؛ كذا في البزازية. وفي الجوهرة : أما المريض الذي لا يمنعه من الحضور فهو كالصحيح ا هـ. وقيد بمدة السفر لأن ما دونها كالحاضر ؛ كذا في الجوهرة. وفي المحيط : إن كان الموكل مريضاً أو مسافراً فالتوكيل منهما لا يلزم بدون رضا الخصم بل يقال للمدعي إن شئت جواب خصمك فاصبر حتى يرتفع العذر، وإن لم تصبر فسبيلك الرضا بالتوكيل فإذا رضي لزمه برضاه في ظاهر الرواية ا هـ. وهو خاص بتوكيل المدعى عليه كما لا يخفى وإرادة السفر أمر باطني فلا بد من دليلها وهو إما تصديق الخصم بها أو القرينة الظاهرة ولا يقبل قوله إني أريد السفر لكن القاضي ينظر في حاله وفي عدته فإنها لا تخفى هيئة من يسافر ؛ كذا ذكره الشارح. وفي البزازية : وإن قال اخرج بالقافلة الفلانية سألهم عنه كما في فسخ الإجارة ا هـ. وفي خزانة المفتين : ولو قال إني أريد السفر يلزم منه التوكيل طالباً كان أو مطلوباً لكن يكفل المطلوب ليتمكن الطالب من استيفاء دينه وإن كذبه الخصم في إرادته السفر يحلفه القاضي بالله أنك تريد السفر ا هـ . وأما المخدرة فهي في اللغة كما في القاموس من الخدر كالإخدار والتخدير بفتح الخاء إلزام البنت الخدر - بكسر الخاء - وهو ستر يمد للجارية في ناحية البيت وهي برد الخصم ؟ عند أبي حنيفة نعم وعندهما لا ،ويجبر واختاره أبو الليث للفتوى اهـ.
His saying: (And for litigation regarding rights with the consent of the opponent unless the principal is sick or absent for the duration of travel or intending to travel or a woman in seclusion) meaning: agency for litigation is valid subject to the opponent's consent, and this is according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is permissible without his consent; there is no dispute about permissibility, only about bindingness. Their proof: agency is a disposition in one's exclusive right, so it does not depend on another's consent, like agency for collecting debts. His proof: the response is due from the opponent, and for this reason he is summoned; people vary in litigation ability; if we say it is binding, he would be harmed, so it depends on his consent, like a jointly owned slave if one of the co-owners contracts kitabah with him, the other has the option. Contrary to the sick and traveler because response is not mandatory upon them there. And the one intending to travel is like him due to necessity. The woman in seclusion: if she were to attend, she could not articulate her right due to her modesty, so her agency is binding; this is something the later scholars deemed as istihsan. Thus in al-Hidayah. Its apparent meaning is that there is no explicit text on the woman in seclusion in the madhhab; for this reason he said in Fath al-Qadir: As for the apparent absolute meaning of the original text and others from Abu Hanifa, there is no difference between a virgin, non-virgin, secluded woman, and non-secluded woman; the fatwa is according to what they chose of that. And khusumah is argumentation; he disputed with him... (linguistic explanation). ...And legally it is the answer with 'yes' or 'no' as will come. And it was interpreted in al-Jawharah as the valid claim or the explicit answer. And if he authorized him in litigation for him not against him, then he has... His saying: (There is no dispute about permissibility, only about bindingness) He said in al-Jawharah: meaning: is the agency rejected? Establishing what belongs to the principal; if the defendant wanted to pay, it would not be heard; thus in Munyat al-Mufti. The conclusion: it is specified by the principal's specification and generalized by his generalization; the definite article in 'rights' is for the genus, so it includes a specific right and all rights. And in al-Qunyah: if he consented then after a day said 'I do not consent,' he has that right. And it was mentioned in Sharh al-Majma' attributing to it, and the restriction to a day is incidental; the point is that he can withdraw consent as long as the judge has not heard the lawsuit. Because in al-Qunyah also: if the agent of the plaintiff claimed before the judge and then brought witnesses to establish it, and the opponent (defendant) does not consent to the agent and wants to litigate with the opponent, he does not have that after hearing the lawsuit according to the position of Abu Hanifa. And in al-Bazzaziyyah: if he authorized him for every right he has and for litigation in every right, and he did not specify the opponent or the subject matter, it is valid. And if he authorized him to collect every right that accrues to him and litigation therein, his authorization is valid; it includes debt, deposit, loan, and every right owned by the principal; as for maintenance, it is among rights he does not own; thus in al-Khazanah. And in al-Walwalijiyyah: if he authorized him for litigation and did not specify which litigation, the agency is not valid because it would involve different genera. And he made 'opponent' absolute, so it includes the plaintiff and defendant as both are included by the principal, and the noble and lowly. And he made 'sick' absolute, which is restricted to when he cannot walk on his feet to the judge's court, whether he is plaintiff or defendant; if he can attend on a riding animal or on a person, then if his sickness increases by that, his agency is binding; if it does not increase, it was said there is dispute, and the correct view is its bindingness; thus in al-Bazzaziyyah. In al-Jawharah: as for the sick person who is not prevented from attending, he is like the healthy. And it was restricted to the duration of travel because less than that is like being present. In al-Muhit: if the principal is sick or traveling, the agency from them is not binding without the opponent's consent; rather it is said to the plaintiff: if you want to respond to your opponent, wait until the excuse is removed, and if you do not wait, your recourse is to consent to the agency; if he consents, it becomes binding by his consent in the apparent narration. This is specific to the agency of the defendant. Intention to travel is internal, so evidence is needed, either the opponent's confirmation or a clear indication; his statement 'I intend to travel' is not accepted, but the judge looks at his condition and preparations, for the appearance of one who travels is not hidden; thus the commentator mentioned. In al-Bazzaziyyah: if he says 'I am leaving with such and such caravan,' he asks about them, as in the cancellation of lease. In Khizanat al-Muftiyyin: if he says 'I intend to travel,' agency becomes necessary from him, whether he is plaintiff or defendant, but the defendant is required to provide a surety so that the plaintiff can recover his debt. If the opponent denies his intention to travel, the judge swears him by Allah that you intend to travel. As for the woman in seclusion, linguistically as in al-Qamus, it comes from al-khidr... (definition)... and she is [protected from] the opponent? According to Abu Hanifa, yes; according to them, no, and he is compelled; Abu al-Layth chose this for fatwa.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding agency in litigation (al-wakalah bi al-khusumah). The matn states that agency in litigation is valid with the opponent's consent, unless the principal is sick, absent for travel duration, intending to travel, or a woman in seclusion. The commentator explains that according to Abu Hanifa, the opponent's consent is required for the agency to be binding, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) hold that the agency is valid and binding without the opponent's consent. The dispute is not about permissibility (everyone agrees it is permissible for the principal to appoint an agent) but about whether the opponent is forced to accept the agent (luzum). The two (Sahibayn) argue that agency is a disposition of one's own right, so it does not require another's consent, analogous to agency for collecting debts. Abu Hanifa argues that the opponent has a right to personally respond to the lawsuit because people vary in litigation skill, and forcing him to accept an agent would cause harm. He draws an analogy to a jointly owned slave: if one co-owner contracts kitabah with him, the other co-owner has the option to accept or reject. However, exceptions are made for the sick and traveler because they are excused from attending court; for the one intending to travel, same ruling. The woman in seclusion (mukhadarah) is an exception added by later scholars via istihsan: if she were to attend court, modesty would prevent her from articulating her case, so her agency is binding. The commentator notes that there is no explicit text in the madhhab about the mukhadarah; some scholars say there is no difference between her and others. The passage then gives linguistic and legal definitions of khusumah. Later it discusses that the opponent can withdraw consent before the judge hears the lawsuit; after that, he cannot. It also details the scope of a general agency for litigation: it includes all rights and any opponent unless specified otherwise. For the sick, the condition is inability to walk to court; if he can ride, he must attend unless it worsens his condition. For the traveler, the intention to travel must be evidenced. The passage concludes with the ruling that the mukhadarah's opponent's consent is required according to Abu Hanifa but not according to the two; Abu al-Layth chose the view that it is required.

Key Terms
خصومة (khusumah): Litigation: the legal process of disputing in court, defined as 'the answer with yes or no' i.e., the formal response to a claim.
مخدرة (mukhadarah): A woman in seclusion (from khidr, a curtain); she is not accustomed to appearing before strangers and thus would be unable to state her case in court due to modesty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, when does agency in litigation become binding on the opponent?
A) It is always binding as soon as the agent accepts.
B) It is binding only if the opponent consents, except when the principal is sick, traveling, or a woman in seclusion.
C) It is binding only if the judge approves the agent.
D) It is never binding; the opponent can always reject the agent.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, agency in litigation is binding only with the opponent's consent, except for the sick, traveler, and woman in seclusion, reflecting a balance between personal right and necessity.

Scope of Agency When Principal Says 'Every Right'
Ruling on scope of agency when principal uses general expression 'every right'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the scope of agency when the principal uses the general expression 'every right' and identify which rights are included and which are excluded according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Agency in 'every right' covers only owned rights; maintenance (nafaqah) is excluded because it is not owned.

In the Book of Agency, the author discusses the scope of an agent's authority when the principal makes a general appointment using the phrase 'every right.' The key principle is that the agent's authority is limited by what the principal owns. This lesson will clarify which rights fall under this umbrella and which do not, particularly focusing on the exclusion of maintenance.

Guided Path
1
Understand the general expression
The principal says 'every right I have' (كل حق). The Arabic uses 'alif-lam' for the genus, which includes all individual rights.
The generality is determined by the principal's wording.
2
Determine the nature of haqq
In this context, haqq refers to rights owned by the principal, such as debt (دين), deposit (وديعة), loan (عارية). Ownership is the key criterion.
Not every claim or entitlement is a haqq; it must be owned.
3
Apply the ownership test
Only rights that the principal owns are included in the agent's authority. The agent can only act on what the principal legally possesses.
This excludes future or contingent rights.
4
Identify the exception
Maintenance (نفقة) is specifically excluded because it is not a right owned by the principal; it becomes due but is not yet owned until actually paid or awarded.
The passage cites al-Khizanah for this exclusion.
5
Note the implication for agency
The agent's authority is thus limited to collecting what the principal owns. He cannot claim maintenance on behalf of the principal, even if it has been ordered by a judge.
This affects litigation and collection strategies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوكالة
إثبات ما للموكل، فلو أراد المدعى عليه الدفع لم تسمع ؛ كذا في منية المفتي. والحاصل أنها تتخصص بتخصيص الموكل وتعمم بتعميمه، والألف واللام في الحقوق للجنس فشمل بعضاً معيناً وجميعها. وفي القنية : لو رضي ثم مضى يوم فقال لا أرضى له ذلك اهـ. وذكره في شرح المجمع معزياً إليها والتقييد باليوم اتفاقي وإنما المقصود أن له الرجوع عن الرضا ما لم يسمع القاضي الدعوى لما في القنية أيضاً : لو ادعى وكيل المدعي عند القاضي ثم أتى بشهود ليقيمها ولم يرض الخصم أي المدعي عليه بالوكيل ويريد أن يخاصم مع الخصم ليس له ذلك بعد سماع الدعوى على أصل أبي حنيفة. وفي البزازية ولو وكله بكل حق هو له وبخصومته. في كل حق له ولم يعين المخاصم به والمخاصم فيه جاز ا هـ . وإذا وكله بقبض كل حق يحدث له والخصومة فيه جائز أمره فإنه يدخل فيه الدين والوديعة والعارية وكل حق ملكه الموكل، أما النفقة فمن الحقوق التي لا يملكها كذا في الخزانة.
Book of Agency. Proving what is for the principal. So if the defendant wants to push back, it is not heard; thus in Munyat al-Mufti. The summary is that it (the agency) becomes specific by the principal's specification and general by his generalization, and the alif and lam in 'rights' are for the genus, so it includes a specific one and all of them. In al-Qunyah: If he agreed, then a day passed and he said 'I do not agree to that', [it is valid]. Mentioned in Sharh al-Majma' attributing to it, and the restriction to a day is accidental, the point is that he has the right to revoke consent as long as the judge has not heard the case. Because in al-Qunyah also: If the agent of the plaintiff claimed before the judge, then brought witnesses to establish it, and the opponent (i.e. defendant) did not consent to the agent and wants to litigate with the opponent, he does not have that after the hearing according to Abu Hanifa. In al-Bazzaziyyah: If he appointed him over every right he has and over his litigation, for every right he has, and he did not specify the one to be litigated against nor the subject of litigation, it is permissible. And if he appointed him to collect every right that accrues to him and litigation over it, his order is permissible, then it includes debt, deposit, loan, and every right owned by the principal. As for maintenance, it is among rights that he does not own, thus in al-Khizanah.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement about the scope of agency when the principal uses a general expression. The author explains that if the principal says 'I appoint you over every right I have,' the agency includes all rights owned by the principal, such as debts, deposits, loans, etc. However, maintenance (nafaqah) is excluded because it is not a right that the principal owns; it is a right that becomes due but is not yet owned. The passage also clarifies that the principal can revoke consent to the agent as long as the judge has not heard the case. Once the case is heard, according to Abu Hanifa, the agent's appointment cannot be objected to by the opponent. The key principle is that the agent's authority is limited by the principal's specification and general by his generalization.

Key Terms
حق (haqq): A right owned by the principal, such as debt, deposit, loan.
نفقة (nafaqah): Maintenance; a right that becomes due but is not owned by the principal.
وكالة (wakalah): Agency; the appointment of an agent to act on behalf of the principal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Loan
D) Maintenance (nafaqah)

Key Takeaway
The agent's authority is limited to rights owned by the principal; maintenance is excluded because it is not owned.

Opponent's Consent When Principal is Ill or Traveling
Ruling on necessity of opponent's consent for agency when principal is ill or traveling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a sick or traveling principal's agency becomes binding without the opponent's consent, and apply them to given scenarios.

Core Idea
A sick or traveling principal needs opponent's consent unless the excuse genuinely prevents attendance.

In Hanafi fiqh, agency (wakalah) in litigation is normally contingent on the opponent's consent when the principal has an excuse. This lesson examines the rulings for a sick or traveling principal, clarifying when the agency is binding and who must consent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principal's excuse
Determine if the principal is claiming illness or travel. The ruling applies only if the principal has a valid excuse: sickness that prevents walking or genuine travel.
The passage distinguishes between the two excuses.
2
Check the condition for sickness
For the sick, verify if he cannot walk to court on foot. If he cannot walk, the agency is binding without consent. If he can walk but illness worsens by attending, still binding.
This is from al-Bazzaziyyah and al-Jawharah.
3
Check the condition for travel
For the traveler, confirm intention to travel with evidence. Mere claim is not enough; the judge looks for preparations or caravan plans. If the opponent denies, the judge administers an oath.
Evidence may be opponent's attestation or apparent preparations.
4
Determine the role of opponent's consent
If the principal can attend despite his excuse (e.g., mild illness or short travel), then opponent's consent is required for the agency to be binding. Otherwise, the opponent can wait until the excuse is removed.
The default rule in al-Muhit: agency is not binding without consent.
5
Apply to a scenario
Use the conditions to decide whether a given concrete case makes the agency binding on the opponent.
Practice with the tasks below.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأطلق في الخصم فشمل الطالب والمطلوب كما شملهما الموكل، والشريف والوضيع كما في البزازية. وأطلق المريض وهو مقيد بما إذا كان لا يقدر على المشي على قدميه إلى مجلس القاضي مدعياً كان أو مدعى عليه، وإن قدر على الحضور على ظهر الدابة أو ظهر إنسان فإن زاد مرضه بذلك لزم توكيله فإن لم يزد قيل على الخلاف والصحيح لزومه؛ كذا في البزازية. وفي الجوهرة : أما المريض الذي لا يمنعه من الحضور فهو كالصحيح ا هـ. وقيد بمدة السفر لأن ما دونها كالحاضر ؛ كذا في الجوهرة. وفي المحيط : إن كان الموكل مريضاً أو مسافراً فالتوكيل منهما لا يلزم بدون رضا الخصم بل يقال للمدعي إن شئت جواب خصمك فاصبر حتى يرتفع العذر، وإن لم تصبر فسبيلك الرضا بالتوكيل فإذا رضي لزمه برضاه في ظاهر الرواية ا هـ. وهو خاص بتوكيل المدعى عليه كما لا يخفى وإرادة السفر أمر باطني فلا بد من دليلها وهو إما تصديق الخصم بها أو القرينة الظاهرة ولا يقبل قوله إني أريد السفر لكن القاضي ينظر في حاله وفي عدته فإنها لا تخفى هيئة من يسافر ؛ كذا ذكره الشارح. وفي البزازية : وإن قال اخرج بالقافلة الفلانية سألهم عنه كما في فسخ الإجارة ا هـ. وفي خزانة المفتين : ولو قال إني أريد السفر يلزم منه التوكيل طالباً كان أو مطلوباً لكن يكفل المطلوب ليتمكن الطالب من استيفاء دينه وإن كذبه الخصم في إرادته السفر يحلفه القاضي بالله أنك تريد السفر ا هـ .
And he (the author) released (the term) regarding the opponent, so it includes the plaintiff and the defendant as they are both included by the principal, and the noble and the lowly as in al-Bazzaziyyah. And he released (the term) regarding the sick person, and it is restricted to when he is unable to walk on his feet to the court of the judge, whether he is plaintiff or defendant. And if he is able to attend on an animal or a person, then if his illness increases by that, his agency becomes binding; if it does not increase, it is said there is a difference of opinion, and the correct view is its binding; thus in al-Bazzaziyyah. In al-Jawharah: As for the sick person whom illness does not prevent from attending, he is like the healthy. So when he consents, it becomes binding upon him by his consent in the apparent narration. And it is specific to the agency of the defendant, as is not hidden. And the intention of travel is an internal matter, so evidence for it is required: either the opponent's attestation to it or an apparent indication. Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement about the conditions under which a sick or traveling principal may appoint an agent without the opponent's consent. According to the Hanafi school, a sick person who cannot walk to court is excused, and his agency is binding without the opponent's consent. However, if he can attend on a mount or with help, the agency is binding only if his illness would worsen; otherwise there is a difference of opinion, but the correct view is that it is still binding. For a traveler, the intention to travel must be evidenced; mere claim is not enough. The judge verifies by looking at his preparations. If the opponent denies the intention, the judge administers an oath. Once the opponent consents, the agency becomes binding. The ruling specifically applies when the agent is the defendant, as the plaintiff cannot force the defendant to accept an agent without the plaintiff's consent.

Key Terms
مريض (marid): A sick person who cannot walk to court on his feet.
مسافر (musafir): A traveler whose intention to travel is proven by evidence.
رضا الخصم (rida al-khasm): Consent of the opponent (defendant) for the plaintiff to appoint an agent.

C) Only if the opponent agrees
D) Only if the judge orders it

Key Takeaway
A sick or traveling principal's agency is binding on the opponent only if the principal cannot attend court or if the opponent consents, with strict conditions for the excuse.

Preferred Opinion on Agency Without Opponent's Consent
Tarjih among Hanafi authorities on agency consent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on agency without opponent's consent, and identify the mufta bihi according to later Hanafi authorities.

Core Idea
Agency without opponent's consent: Imam says non-binding, Sahibayn say binding, later fatwa leans to Sahibayn.

In Hanafi fiqh, when a defendant appoints an agent without the plaintiff's consent, does the agency bind the opponent? The school's founding imams differed. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq surveys the later tarjih (preference) among Hanafi authorities, showing how the mufta bihi shifted over time. Understanding this intra-madhhab evolution is key to navigating fatwa in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
What is the exact legal issue? Agency (tawkeel) by the defendant without the opponent's (plaintiff's) consent. Does the opponent have to accept the agent?
2
State the two positions
Imam Abu Hanifa: agency is not binding (the opponent can reject). Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): agency is binding (opponent must deal with the agent).
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Survey the later authorities
The passage lists scholars and their tarjih: al-Faqih, al-Ghiya'i, al-Saffar, Khizanat al-Muftin, al-Nihayah all prefer Sahibayn. Al-Halwani gives the mufti a choice. Al-Bazzaziyyah notes that delegating to judges is not reliable in corrupt times.
4
Determine the operative position (mufta bihi)
According to most cited authorities, the mufta bihi is the view of Sahibayn: agency without opponent's consent is binding.
But note al-Halwani's opinion and the warning about judges.
5
Understand the thamarah (practical consequence)
If mufta bihi is Sahibayn, then the defendant can appoint an agent and the plaintiff must accept it; if the Imam's view is followed, the plaintiff can refuse and demand the defendant appear personally.
This affects court procedure and convenience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن المؤلف اختار قول الإمام كما هو دأبه، وقد اختلف ترجيح المشايخ فأفتى الفقيه بقولهما. وقال الغيائي: وهو المختار وبه أخذ الصفار أيضاً. وفي خزانة المفتين : المختار قولهما والشريف وغيره سواء. وفي النهاية والصحيح قولهما. وقال الحلواني : يخير المفتي قال: ونحن نفتي أن الرأي للحاكم. وفي البزازية ومن المعلوم المقرر أن تفويض الخيار إلى قضاة عهد الفساد كما هو المقرر من أن علمهم ليس بحجة. قال شمس الأئمة :
Then know that the author chose the statement of the Imam as is his wont, and the preference of the scholars differed: al-Faqih gave fatwa according to their statement (Sahibayn). Al-Ghiya'i said: It is the chosen one, and al-Saffar also adopted it. In Khizanat al-Muftin: The chosen one is their statement, and al-Sharif and others are equal. In al-Nihayah: And the correct is their statement. Al-Halwani said: The mufti is given a choice; he said: And we give fatwa that the opinion is of the judge. In al-Bazzaziyyah: And it is known and established that delegating the choice to judges in an age of corruption is as established that their knowledge is not authoritative. Shams al-Aimmah said:
Source pages p. 245

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about which opinion is preferred regarding the binding of agency without the opponent's consent. The author (presumably of the sharh) chose the opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa (that agency without consent is not binding). However, many later scholars (mashayikh) preferred the opinion of the two disciples (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that it is binding. Al-Ghiya'i and al-Saffar preferred their statement. Khizanat al-Muftin also chose the statement of the two. In al-Nihayah, the correct view is that of the two. Al-Halwani said the mufti may choose, and his own opinion is that the judge should decide. There is a note from al-Bazzaziyyah that delegating choice to judges in corrupt times is problematic because their knowledge may not be authoritative. The passage ends abruptly with Shams al-Aimmah beginning to speak. This indicates a difference of opinion among Hanafi authorities, and the student should know that the relied-upon fatwa may vary by region and period.

Key Terms
قول الإمام (qawl al-imam): The opinion of Abu Hanifa that agency without opponent's consent is not binding.
قولهما (qawlihima): The opinion of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) that agency without consent is binding.
المختار (al-mukhtar): The chosen or preferred opinion for fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa
B) The opinion of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn)
C) The judge's discretion
D) The mufti's choice

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in later Hanafi fatwa is the Sahibayn's view: agency is binding even without the opponent's consent, though the Imam's view remains part of the school's heritage.

Evidence of Agency in Hanafi Litigation
Rules for agent in litigation and proof of agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the condition that evidence (bayyinah) is only accepted against an adversary (khasm) in cases of agency for debt collection.

Core Idea
Evidence is only accepted against an adversary; acknowledging agency does not acknowledge the debt.

This lesson unpacks a procedural rule from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: the agent in litigation cannot sue before a different jurist than the one designated, and more importantly, the proof of agency via witnesses hinges on the presence of a proper adversary. We will explore how Hanafi jurists distinguish cases where evidence is admissible versus rejected, using examples from Qadikhan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on venue limitation
The passage states that if the principal appoints an agent to sue before a specific jurist, the agent cannot sue before another jurist unless that other is a general judge, because the first jurist is a designated arbiter (hakam), not the general judge.
General judges have inherent authority; appointed arbiters do not.
2
Extract the general principle on evidence
The text says: 'al-bayyinah la tuqbal illa 'ala khasm' — evidence is only accepted against an adversary. This is the key procedural rule.
No adversary means no valid evidence.
3
Apply the principle to the first scenario
If the debtor acknowledges the agency but denies the debt, the agent cannot prove the debt by witnesses because the debtor, by denying the debt, is not an adversary for the debt claim. The agency is not yet proven, so the debtor is not a proper adversary.
The acknowledgment of agency does not make him an adversary for the debt.
4
Apply the principle to the second scenario
If the debtor acknowledges agency and the agent fears the principal will appear and deny the agency, then the agent can produce evidence to prove the agency, because now the adversary (the principal) is or will be present.
The evidence is against the principal, not the debtor.
5
Distinguish similar cases
The passage likens the rule to cases of executorship and inheritance: when the debtor acknowledges the executor's role but denies the debt, the executor can prove executorship with evidence. Similarly, a claimant against a deceased who presents an heir that acknowledges the debt can then prove the debt with evidence, as the heir is an adversary.
In those cases, the adversary exists (the heir or the debtor for the role).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لم يكن له أن يخاصمه إلى فقيه آخر) كان وجهه أنه جعل هذا الفقيه حكماً فلا يكون الآخر حكماً بدون أمره بخلاف القاضي الآخر فإن ولايته ثابتة وإن لم يأمر تأمل. قوله: (والقاضي) معطوف على الصبي قوله : ثم اعلم أن طريق إثبات الوكالة الخ) قال قاضيخان وكله بقبض فأقر المديون بوكالته وأنكر الدين فبرهن عليه الوكيل لا يقبل إذ البينة لا تقبل إلا على خصم، وبإقرار المديون لم تثبت الوكالة فلم يكن خصماً ألا ترى أنه لو أقر بالوكالة فقال الوكيل إني أبرهن على وكالتي مخافة أن يحضر الطالب وينكر الوكالة تقبل بينته ولو قامت على المقر، أقر المديون بوصايته وأنكر الدين فأثبت الوصي وصايته ببينة تقبل، وكذا من ادعى ديناً على الميت وأحضر وارثاً فأقر الوارث بالدين فقال المدعي أنا أثبت ببينة فبرهن يقبل. نور العين. وكذا وصي
His saying: (He may not sue him before another jurist) The reasoning is that he made this jurist an arbiter, so another jurist cannot be arbiter without his permission, unlike another judge because his authority is established even without permission. Contemplate. His saying: (And the judge) is conjoined to the boy. Then know that the method of proving agency (etc.). Qadikhan said: He appointed him to collect a debt, the debtor acknowledged his agency but denied the debt, so the agent produced evidence; it is not accepted because evidence is only accepted against an adversary. By the debtor's acknowledgment, the agency was not established, so he is not an adversary. Do you not see that if he acknowledged agency, and the agent said, 'I will produce evidence of my agency out of fear that the claimant will appear and deny the agency,' his evidence is accepted even if it stands against the acknowledger. The debtor acknowledged his executorship and denied the debt, so the executor proved his executorship with evidence – it is accepted. Similarly, if one claims a debt against the deceased and produces an heir, the heir acknowledges the debt, and the claimant says, 'I will prove it with evidence,' then he proves it – it is accepted. Nur al-Ayn. Similarly, an executor.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage discusses two related topics: first, the agent in litigation (الوكيل بالخصومة) and the restriction that if the principal appoints him to sue before a specific jurist (scholar), he cannot sue before another jurist because that jurist is considered a designated arbiter. However, if the principal appoints him for a specific judge, he can sue before another judge because the judge's authority is general. Second, the passage explains the method of proving agency in court. The key principle is that evidence (baina) is only accepted against an adversary (khasm). If the debtor acknowledges the agency, that does not make him an adversary for proving the debt; the agent cannot then produce evidence to prove the debt because the debtor's acknowledgment of agency is not an acknowledgment of the debt. The commentator provides several examples from Qadikhan to illustrate when evidence is or is not accepted, emphasizing that the presence of an adversary is crucial.

Key Terms
وكيل بالخصومة (wakil bi al-khusumah): An agent appointed to represent the principal in litigation before a judge.
خصم (khasm): Adversary or opposing party in a legal dispute.
بينة (bayyinah): Legal evidence, typically testimony of two witnesses or other proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is evidence (bayyinah) for agency accepted?
A) When the debtor acknowledges the agency and the debt.
B) When the agent produces evidence in the presence of an adversary.
C) When the agent is the executor of a will.
D) When the judge orders it.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi procedural law, evidence of agency is admissible only when presented against a proper adversary; mere acknowledgment of the agency does not create an adversary for the underlying claim.

Rulings on the Agent Appointed to Pay or Receive a Debt
Detailed rulings on two types of debt agency with proofs and analogies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for an agent appointed to pay a debt from his own money and an agent appointed to receive a debt, and explain the conditions for the agent's reimbursement and the principal's recourse.

Core Idea
An agent who pays a debt from his own money is like a buyer; he is not reimbursed until the debt is actually discharged.

Agency in debt transactions is common. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details two types: the agent who pays and the agent who receives. Understanding the agent's right to reimbursement and the reliability of his statements is crucial for both parties. We will examine the scenarios where the principal confirms payment but the creditor denies it, and the rules for setoff when the agent also owes the debtor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of agents
The passage explicitly distinguishes between an agent appointed to pay a debt (وكيل بقضاء الدين) and an agent appointed to receive a debt (وكيل بقبض الدين). Note the different rules for each.
2
Analyze the first scenario: agent pays, principal confirms, creditor denies
If the agent claims payment and the principal confirms, but later the creditor denies and takes from the principal, the principal must still repay the agent. The principal can then recourse against the agent.
This is the ruling despite the principal's initial confirmation.
3
Understand the qiyas analogy to a buyer
The correct view likens the agent to a buyer who pays the price only after receiving the purchased item. The agent does not secure discharge until the creditor actually receives payment; thus reimbursement is conditional on actual discharge.
This explains why the agent cannot recourse if the principal confirms but the creditor later denies.
4
Analyze the second type: agent for receipt
The agent for receipt is trusted regarding his statements about receipt, loss, and delivery to the principal. The debtor is discharged even if the agent is not a credible witness for himself.
Contrast with the agent for payment, whose statements about payment are not automatically accepted against the creditor.
5
Note the setoff rule
If the agent for receipt owes a debt to the principal's debtor, setoff (مقاصة) occurs, and the agent becomes the principal's debtor for that amount.
This simplifies transactions by automatically cancelling mutual debts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يرجع ووفيته إياه بالتثقيل ؛ كذا في المصباح والمراد به هنا دفع ما عليه والاستيفاء والتوفي بمعنى واحد كما في المصباح. والمراد به هنا القبض فكأنه يقول صح التوكيل بدفع ما عليه ويقبض ماله. أما الأول فمن مسائله قالوا لو وكله بقضاء الدين فجاء الوكيل وزعم قضاءه وصدقه موكله فيه فلما طالبه وكيله برد ما قضاه لأجله قال الموكل أخاف أن يحضر الدائن وينكر قضاء وكيلي ويأخذه مني ثانياً لا يلتفت إلى قول الموكل ويؤمر بالخروج عن حق وكيله، فإذا حضر الدائن وأخذ من الموكل يرجع الموكل على الوكيل بما دفعه إليه وإن كان صدقه بالقضاء. وفي كتاب الحوالة : أمره بقضاء دينه فقال قضيت وصدقه الآمر فيه ثم حلف الدائن على عدم وصوله إليه وأخذه المأمور على الأمر لأن الأمر كذب في إقراره حيث الأمر لا من قضى عليه بالدين لأن الإقرار إنما يبطل بالحكم على خلافه إذا كان الحكم بالبينة أما بغيرها فلا، والصحيح أنه يعلل لعدم رجوع المأمور على الآمر بأن المأمور وكيل بشراء ما في ذمة الأمر بمثله ونقد الثمن من مال نفسه وإنما يرجع على الأمر إذا سلم له ما في ذمته كالمشتري إنما يؤمر بتسليم الثمن إلى الآمر إذا سلم للآمر ما اشترى، أما إذا لم يسلم فلا . وذكر أن ر على المأمور والمأمور يرجع على المديون بما قضى. قال قضيت رب الدين يرجع دينك بأمرك لفلان فأنكر كونه مديون فلان وأمره وقضاه أيضاً والدائن غائب فبرهن المأمور على الدين والأمر والقضاء يحكم بالكل لأن الدائن وإن كان غائباً لكنه عنه خصم حاضر فإن المدعي على الغائب سبب لما يدعي على الحاضر لأنه ما لم يقض دينه لا يجب له عليه شيء وبينهما اتصال أيضاً الأمر وبعد السببية والاتصال ينتصب خصماً، ولو قال لا تدفع وهو الدين إلا بمحضر فلان ففعل بلا محضره ضمن ؛ كذا في البزازية ولو ادعى الوكيل أنه دفع بمحضره أو قال لا تدفع إلا بشهود فادعى دفعة بشهود وأنكر الدائن القبض حلف الوكيل أنه دفع بشهود، فإذا حلف لم يضمن ؛ كذا في كافي الحاكم . ولو قال ادفعه بشهود فدفع بغيرهم لم يضمن. وأما الثاني أعني الوكيل بقبض الدين فيقبل قوله في قبضه وضياعه ودفعه إلى الموكل ويبرأ الغريم ولو كان ممن لا تقبل شهادته للوكيل بخلاف إقراره بقبض الطالب، ولو وجب على الوكيل بالقبض مثله لمديون موكله وقعت المقاصة وكان الوكيل مديون الموكل.
He returns. And 'wafaituhu iyyahu' with tathqil; thus in al-Misbah. What is meant here is payment of what is owed, and al-istifa' and al-tawfi have one meaning as in al-Misbah. What is meant here is receipt, so it is as if he says: agency is valid for paying what is owed and receiving his property. As for the first, from its issues, they said: if he appointed him to pay a debt, and the agent came and claimed he paid it, and his principal confirmed him in that, then when his agent demanded him to repay what he paid for him, the principal said: 'I fear that the creditor will come and deny my agent's payment and take it from me a second time,' – his statement is not heeded, and he is ordered to fulfill his agent's right. If the creditor then comes and takes from the principal, the principal may recourse against the agent for what he paid him even though he confirmed his payment. In Kitab al-Hawalah: He ordered him to pay his debt, so he said 'I paid,' and the orderer confirmed him, then the creditor swore that he did not receive it and took it from the agent, the agent cannot recourse against the orderer because the orderer is lying in his acknowledgment – but the orderer is not one against whom the debt has been judged, because acknowledgment is only invalidated by a ruling contrary to it if the ruling is based on evidence, otherwise not. The correct view is that it is explained that the agent does not recourse against the orderer because the agent is an agent for purchasing what is in the orderer's liability with its equivalent and paying the price from his own money; he only recourses against the orderer if he hands over to him what is in his liability, like the buyer, who is only commanded to pay the price to the orderer if the orderer hands over what he bought. If he does not hand over, then no. And it is mentioned that he recourses against the agent, and the agent recourses against the debtor for what he paid. He said: 'I paid, Lord of the debt, your debt by your order to so-and-so,' but he denied being a debtor to so-and-so, and he ordered and paid also while the creditor was absent, so the agent proved the debt, the order, and the payment, and the judge rules all, because even though the creditor is absent, there is a present adversary for him, for the claimant against the absent has a cause for what he claims against the present, because if he had not paid his debt, nothing would be due from him, and there is also connection through the order; after causation and connection, he becomes an adversary. And if he said, 'Do not pay the debt except in the presence of so-and-so,' and he did without his presence, he is liable. Thus in al-Bazzaziyyah. If the agent claimed that he paid in his presence, or said, 'Do not pay except with witnesses,' and he claimed payment with witnesses, and the creditor denied receipt, the agent swears that he paid with witnesses; if he swears, he is not liable. Thus in Kafi al-Hakim. If he said, 'Pay him with witnesses,' and he paid without them, he is not liable. As for the second, namely the agent for receipt of the debt, his statement is accepted regarding its receipt, loss, and delivery to the principal, and the debtor is discharged, even if he is someone whose testimony is not accepted for the agent, unlike his acknowledgment of receipt by the claimant. If a like amount is owed by the agent for receipt to the principal's debtor, setoff occurs, and the agent becomes the principal's debtor.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage provides detailed rulings on two types of debt-related agency. First, the agent appointed to pay a debt (وكيل بقضاء الدين) who pays from his own money. If the agent claims payment, the principal confirms, but later the creditor denies and takes from the principal, the principal cannot refuse to repay the agent; the agent is entitled to reimbursement. However, if the principal had ordered a third party to pay the debt, and that third party (the agent) paid and the principal confirmed, but the creditor swore non-receipt and took from the agent, the agent cannot recourse against the principal because the agent is considered to have bought the debt and paid its price; he only recourses if he actually discharges the debt. There are also rules about paying in front of a specified person or witnesses. Second, the agent for receipt of debt (وكيل بقبض الدين) – his statement about receipt, loss, and delivery to principal is accepted, and the debtor is discharged. However, if the agent owes a debt to the principal's debtor, setoff occurs and the agent becomes debtor to his principal. The commentary relies on various sources like al-Bazzaziyyah, Kafi al-Hakim, and Kitab al-Hawalah.

Key Terms
وكيل بقضاء الدين (wakil bi qada' al-dayn): An agent appointed to pay a debt on behalf of the principal, usually from the agent's own money.
وكيل بقبض الدين (wakil bi qabd al-dayn): An agent appointed to receive a debt from the debtor on behalf of the principal.
مقاصة (muqasah): Setoff of mutual debts; when two parties owe each other, the debts cancel to the extent of the smaller.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if an agent appointed to pay a debt claims payment and the principal confirms, but later the creditor denies and takes payment from the principal, what is the ruling?
A) The principal cannot recourse against the agent.
B) The principal can recourse against the agent for what he paid him.
C) The agent is not liable and the creditor must return the money.
D) The principal must pay the creditor and cannot take from the agent.

Key Takeaway
An agent who pays a debt from his own money is treated like a buyer: reimbursement is due only when the debt is actually discharged; whereas an agent for receipt is trusted for his statements about receipt and delivery.
